)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedtoprow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         Highest\xc2\xa0elevation\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         144\xc2\xa0ft (34\xc2\xa0m)\n href="/wiki/File:Hampton_Roads_(Virginia)_-_Location.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="344" data-file-width="792" height="152" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Hampton_Roads_%28Virginia%29_-_Location.svg/700px-Hampton_Roads_%28Virginia%29_-_Location.svg.png 2x" width="350"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hampton_Roads_(Virginia)_-_Location.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Hampton Roads\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Hampton Roads\n       </b>\n       is the name of both a body of water in Virginia and the surrounding metropolitan region in Southeastern Virginia and Northeastern North Carolina, United States. Comprising the\n       <a href="#Definitions">\n        Virginia Beach\xe2\x80\x93Norfolk\xe2\x80\x93Newport News, VA\xe2\x80\x93NC\n       </a>\n       metropolitan area and an extended\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Combined Statistical Area">\n        Combined Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       that includes the\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_City,_North_Carolina_micropolitan_area" title="Elizabeth City, North Carolina micropolitan area">\n        Elizabeth City, NC Micropolitan Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Dare_County,_North_Carolina" title="Dare County, North Carolina">\n        Kill Devil Hills, NC Micropolitan Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       , Hampton Roads is known for its large military presence, ice-free harbor, shipyards,\n       <a href="/wiki/Coal_pier" title="Coal pier">\n        coal piers\n       </a>\n       , and miles of waterfront property and beaches, all of which contribute to the diversity and stability of the region\'s economy.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The body of water known as Hampton Roads is one of the world\'s largest natural\n       <a href="/wiki/Harbor" title="Harbor">\n        harbors\n       </a>\n       (more accurately a\n       <a href="/wiki/Roadstead" title="Roadstead">\n        roadstead\n       </a>\n       or "roads"). It incorporates the mouths of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_River_(Virginia)" title="Elizabeth River (Virginia)">\n        Elizabeth River\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nansemond_River" title="Nansemond River">\n        Nansemond River\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/James_River" title="James River">\n        James River\n       </a>\n       with several smaller rivers and empties into the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       near its mouth leading to the Atlantic Ocean.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The land area (also known as "\n       <a href="/wiki/Tidewater_region" title="Tidewater region">\n        Tidewater\n       </a>\n       "\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_1-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ) includes a collection of cities, counties and towns on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Peninsula" title="Virginia Peninsula">\n        Virginia Peninsula\n       </a>\n       and in\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Hampton_Roads" title="South Hampton Roads">\n        South Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n       . Some of the outlying areas further from the harbor may or may not be included as part of "Hampton Roads", depending upon the organization or usage. For example, as defined for federal economic purposes, the Hampton Roads metropolitan statistical area (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">\n        MSA\n       </a>\n       ) includes two counties in northeastern\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">\n        North Carolina\n       </a>\n       and two counties in Virginia\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Peninsula" title="Middle Peninsula">\n        Middle Peninsula\n       </a>\n       . The Virginia Beach\xe2\x80\x93Norfolk\xe2\x80\x93Newport News, VA\xe2\x80\x93NC MSA has a population of over 1.7\xc2\xa0million, making it the 37th-largest metropolitan area in the United States and the largest on the Eastern Seaboard between New York and Miami.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Combined Statistical Area">\n        Combined Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       includes four additional counties in North Carolina, pushing the regional population to over 1.8 million residents, the 32nd largest\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Combined Statistical Area">\n        CSA\n       </a>\n       in the country.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The area is steeped in 400 years of American history, with hundreds of historical sites and attractions that draw visitors from around the world each year. The harbor was the key to Hampton Roads\' growth, both on land and in water-related activities and events. While the harbor and its tributaries were (and still are) important transportation conduits, at the same time they presented obstacles to land-based commerce and travel.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Creating and maintaining adequate infrastructure has long been a major challenge. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads_Bridge%E2%80%93Tunnel" title="Hampton Roads Bridge\xe2\x80\x93Tunnel">\n        Hampton Roads Bridge\xe2\x80\x93Tunnel\n       </a>\n       (HRBT) and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Monitor%E2%80%93Merrimac_Memorial_Bridge%E2%80%93Tunnel" title="Monitor\xe2\x80\x93Merrimac Memorial Bridge\xe2\x80\x93Tunnel">\n        Monitor\xe2\x80\x93Merrimac Memorial Bridge\xe2\x80\x93Tunnel\n       </a>\n       (MMMBT) are major harbor crossings of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads_Beltway" title="Hampton Roads Beltway">\n        Hampton Roads Beltway\n       </a>\n       interstate, which links the large population centers of Hampton Roads. In 2007, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads_Transportation_Authority" title="Hampton Roads Transportation Authority">\n        Hampton Roads Transportation Authority\n       </a>\n       (HRTA) was formed under a controversial state law to levy various additional taxes, fees, and tolls to generate funding for major regional transportation projects, including a long-sought but costly third crossing of the harbor of Hampton Roads.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#Etymology">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span Counties and independent cities\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-4">\n             <a href="#In_Virginia">\n              <span   </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-47">\n           <a href="#Magazines">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             15.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Magazines\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-48">\n           <a href="#Television">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             15.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Television\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-49">\n           <a href="#Radio">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             15.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Radio\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-50">\n         <a href="#Sports">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           16\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Sports\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-51">\n           <a href="#Team_sports">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             16.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Team sports\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-52">\n           <a href="#Individual_sports">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             16.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Individual sports\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 <span class="tocnumber">\n           17\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-55">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           18\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-56">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           19\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">\n        Etymology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The term "Hampton Roads" is a centuries-old designation that originated when the region was a struggling\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">\n        English\n       </a>\n       outpost nearly four hundred years ago.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The word "Hampton" honors one of the founders of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Company_of_London" title="Virginia Company of London">\n        Virginia Company of London\n       </a>\n       and a great supporter of the colonization of Virginia,\n       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Wriothesley,_3rd_Earl_of_Southampton" title="Henry Wriothesley, 3rd Earl of Southampton">\n        Henry Wriothesley, 3rd Earl of Southampton\n       </a>\n       . The early administrative center of the new colony was known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_City_(Virginia_Company)" title="Elizabeth City (Virginia Company)">\n        Elizabeth Cittie\n       </a>\n       , named for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Bohemia" title="Elizabeth of Bohemia">\n        Princess Elizabeth\n       </a>\n       , the daughter of King James I, and formally designated by the Virginia Company in 1619. The town at the center of Elizabeth Cittie became known as "Hampton", and a nearby waterway was designated Hampton Creek (also known as Hampton River).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other references to the Earl include the area to the north across the bay (in what is now the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Virginia" title="Eastern Shore of Virginia">\n        Eastern Shore\n       </a>\n       ) which became known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Northampton_County,_Virginia" title="Northampton County, Virginia">\n        Northampton\n       </a>\n       , and an area south of the James River which became\n       <a href="/wiki/Southampton_County,_Virginia" title="Southampton County, Virginia">\n        Southampton\n       </a>\n       . As with Hampton, both of these names remain in use today.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The term "Roads" (short for\n       <a href="/wiki/Roadstead" title="Roadstead">\n        roadstead\n       </a>\n       ) indicates the safety of a port; as applied to a body of water, it is "a partly sheltered area of water near a shore in which vessels may ride at anchor".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Examples of other roadsteads are\n       <a href="/wiki/Castle_Roads" title="Castle Roads">\n        Castle Roads\n       </a>\n       , in another of the\n       <a href="/wiki/London_Company" title="London Company">\n        Virginia Company\'s\n       </a>\n       settlements,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">\n        Bermuda\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lahaina_Roads" title="Lahaina Roads">\n        Lahaina Roads\n       </a>\n       , in Hawaii.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1755, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">\n        Virginia General Assembly\n       </a>\n       recorded the name "Hampton Roads" as the channel linking the James, Elizabeth, and Nansemond rivers with the Chesapeake Bay.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_1-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Hampton Roads has become known as the world\'s largest natural harbor\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       , in part because it is the northernmost major East Coast port of the United States which is ice-free year round. (This status is claimed with the notable exception of the extraordinarily cold winter of 1917, which was the entire U.S.\'s coldest year on record.)\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Over time, the entire region has come to be known as "Hampton Roads", a label more specific than its other moniker, "Tidewater Virginia", which could, by implication, include other areas of tidal land in eastern Virginia. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Postal_Service" title="U.S. Postal Service">\n        U.S. Postal Service\n       </a>\n       changed the area\'s postmark from "Tidewater Virginia" to "Hampton Roads, Virginia" beginning in 1983.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_1-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">\n        Definitions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Definitions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Counties_and_independent_cities">\n        Counties and independent cities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Counties and independent cities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The U.S. Census Bureau defines the "Virginia Beach\xe2\x80\x93Norfolk\xe2\x80\x93Newport News, VA\xe2\x80\x93NC MSA" as 16 county-level jurisdictions\xe2\x80\x94five counties and nine independent cities in Virginia, and two counties in North Carolina. While the borders of what locals call "Hampton Roads" may not perfectly align with the definition of the MSA, Hampton Roads is most often the name used for the metropolitan area.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       "Virginia Beach\xe2\x80\x93Norfolk\xe2\x80\x93Newport News, VA\xe2\x80\x93NC MSA" is a U.S.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">\n        Metropolitan Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       (MSA). According to the 2010 Census, its population is 1,676,822\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the 2014 estimated population is 1,716,624.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Since a state constitutional change in 1871, all cities in\n        <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n         Virginia\n        </a>\n        are\n        <a href="/wiki/Independent_city" title="Independent city">\n         independent cities\n        </a>\n        and they are not legally located in a county. The\n        <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">\n         OMB\n        </a>\n        considers these independent cities to be\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/County-equivalent" title="County-equivalent">\n         county-equivalents\n        </a>\n        for the purpose of defining MSAs in Virginia. Each MSA is listed by its counties, then cities, in alphabetical order and not by size.\n       </i>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_Virginia">\n        In Virginia\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: In Virginia">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The MSA consists of these locations in Virginia:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_County,_Virginia" title="Gloucester County, Virginia">\n         Gloucester County\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight_County,_Virginia" title="Isle of Wight County, Virginia">\n         Isle of Wight County\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/James_City_County,_Virginia" title="James City County, Virginia">\n         James City County\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Mathews_County,_Virginia" title="Mathews County, Virginia">\n         Mathews County\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/York_County,_Virginia" title="York County, Virginia">\n         York County\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake,_Virginia" title="Chesapeake, Virginia">\n         City of Chesapeake\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Virginia" title="Hampton, Virginia">\n         City of Hampton\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">\n         City of Newport News\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">\n         City of Norfolk\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Poquoson,_Virginia" title="Poquoson, Virginia">\n         City of Poquoson\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">\n         City of Portsmouth\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Suffolk,_Virginia" title="Suffolk, Virginia">\n         City of Suffolk\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach" title="Virginia Beach">\n         City of Virginia Beach\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n         City of Williamsburg\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_North_Carolina">\n        In North Carolina\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: In North Carolina">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The MSA also includes the following locations in North Carolina:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Currituck_County,_North_Carolina" title="Currituck County, North Carolina">\n         Currituck County\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Gates_County,_North_Carolina" title="Gates County, North Carolina">\n         Gates County\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution_of_Hampton_Roads">\n        Evolution of Hampton Roads\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Evolution of Hampton Roads">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Hampton Roads metropolitan area was first defined in 1950 as the "Norfolk\xe2\x80\x93Portsmouth Metropolitan Statistical Area". It comprised the independent cities of Norfolk, Portsmouth and\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Norfolk,_Virginia" title="South Norfolk, Virginia">\n        South Norfolk\n       </a>\n       and the counties of\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_County,_Virginia" title="Norfolk County, Virginia">\n        Norfolk\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Anne_County" title="Princess Anne County">\n        Princess Anne\n       </a>\n       . In 1952, Virginia Beach separated from Princess Anne County.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1963, Virginia Beach and Princess Anne County merged, retaining the name Virginia Beach. The city was added to the MSA that year, while South Norfolk lost its metropolitan status. Also in 1963, Norfolk County and the City of South Norfolk merged to create the city of Chesapeake.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1970, Chesapeake was added to the MSA\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , while Virginia Beach became a primary city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1973, Currituck County, North Carolina was added to the MSA.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1983, the "Newport News\xe2\x80\x93Hampton Metropolitan Statistical Area", comprising the cities of Newport News, Hampton, Poquoson and Williamsburg, and the counties of Gloucester, James City and York, was combined with the Norfolk\xe2\x80\x93Virginia Beach\xe2\x80\x93Portsmouth MSA and renamed the "Norfolk\xe2\x80\x93Virginia Beach\xe2\x80\x93Newport News MSA".\n      </p>\n      <table class="infobox" style="float: right; font-size:90%">\n       <tr>\n        <th align="center" colspan="11" style="background-color: </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <br/>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <br/>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1993, Isle of Wight, Mathews and Surry counties were added. Although Virginia Beach had passed Norfolk as the state\'s largest city by 1990, it was not made the first primary city of the MSA until 2010.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As a result of the 2010 Census, Gates County, North Carolina was added to the MSA, while\n       <a href="/wiki/Surry_County,_Virginia" title="Surry County, Virginia">\n        Surry County, Virginia\n       </a>\n       was removed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="infobox" style="float: right;     </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         9,207\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         8,978\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         8,782\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="right">\n         -\n        </td>\n        <td align="left">\n         -\n        </td>\n        <td align="left">\n         <a </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         6,829\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         -\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         -\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         -\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         -\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         -\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="right">\n         -\n        </td>\n        <td align="left">\n         -\n        </td>\n        <td align="left">\n         <a href="/wiki/Princess_Anne_County,_Virginia"      </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         -\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         -\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         -\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n </b>\n        </td>\n        <td align="right" style="background-color: #cfb;">\n        </td>\n        <td align="right" style="background-color: #cfb;">\n         445,800\n        </td>\n        <td align="right" style="background-color: #cfb;">\n         579,510\n        </td>\n        <td align="right" style="background-color: #cfb;">\n         680,600\n        </td>\n        <td align="right" style="background-color: #cfb;">\n         806,951\n        </td>\n        <td align="right" style="background-color: #cfb;">\n         1,443,715\n        </td>\n        <td align="right" style="background-color: #cfb;">\n         1,576,370\n        </td>\n        <td align="right" style="background-color: #cfb;">\n         1,676,822\n        </td>\n        <td align="right" style="background-color: #cfb;">\n         1,726,907\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Combined_Statistical_Area">\n        Combined Statistical Area\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Combined Statistical Area">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Virginia Beach\xe2\x80\x93Norfolk, VA\xe2\x80\x93NC\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Combined Statistical Area">\n        Combined Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       additionally includes the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_City,_North_Carolina_Micropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Elizabeth City, North Carolina Micropolitan Statistical Area">\n        Elizabeth City, North Carolina Micropolitan Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       , comprising:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Pasquotank_County,_North_Carolina" title="Pasquotank County, North Carolina">\n         Pasquotank County\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Perquimans_County,_North_Carolina" title="Perquimans County, North Carolina">\n         Perquimans County\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Camden_County,_North_Carolina" title="Camden County, North Carolina">\n         Camden County\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kill_Devil_Hills,_North_Carolina" title="Kill Devil Hills, North Carolina">\n        Kill Devil Hills, North Carolina\n       </a>\n       Micropolitan Statistical Area, comprising:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Dare_County,_North_Carolina" title="Dare County, North Carolina">\n         Dare County\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       As of the 2010 census, the total population of this\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Combined Statistical Area">\n        Combined Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       was 1,779,243, with a 2013 estimate of 1,810,266, a growth of 1.74%. It is currently the 32nd largest in the country and the 2nd largest in Virginia, after the Northern Virginia portion of the Washington, D.C.\xe2\x80\x93Arlington\xe2\x80\x93Alexandria, DC\xe2\x80\x93VA\xe2\x80\x93MD\xe2\x80\x93WV MSA.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Hampton_Roads" title="History of Hampton Roads">\n        History of Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hampton_Roads_1859.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Hampton_Roads_1859.jpg/250px-Hampton_Roads_1859.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Hampton_Roads_1859.jpg/375px-Hampton_Roads_1859.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Hampton_Roads_1859.jpg/500px-Hampton_Roads_1859.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hampton_Roads_1859.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The harbor area of Hampton Roads, from official state map of pre-civil war Virginia circa 1858.\n         <i>\n          image from the Library of Virginia\n         </i>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="17th\xe2\x80\x9319th_centuries">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="17th.E2.80.9319th_centuries">\n        17th\xe2\x80\x9319th centuries\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 17th\xe2\x80\x9319th centuries">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The first colonists arrived in 1607 when English\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Newport" title="Christopher Newport">\n        Captain Christopher Newport\n       </a>\n       landed at\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Henry" title="Cape Henry">\n        Cape Henry\n       </a>\n       , today\'s City of Virginia Beach, an event now called the "First Landing." However, his party moved on, in search of a more defensible area upriver, mindful of competitors such as the Spanish, who had built a failed settlement on the Virginia Peninsula known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ajac%C3%A1n_Mission" title="Ajac\xc3\xa1n Mission">\n        Ajac\xc3\xa1n Mission\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After exploring the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_River_(Virginia)" title="James River (Virginia)">\n        James River\n       </a>\n       , they established the first successful English colony in the\n       <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">\n        New World\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamestown_Island" title="Jamestown Island">\n        Jamestown Island\n       </a>\n       on May 14, 1607.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apva.org_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-apva.org-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       But the low, marshy site proved unhealthy and most of the colonists died, before a new Governor,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_De_La_Warr" title="Lord De La Warr">\n        Lord De La Warr\n       </a>\n       (Delaware) arrived with\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Rolfe" title="John Rolfe">\n        John Rolfe\n       </a>\n       , who would establish the Virginia tobacco industry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apva.org_19-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-apva.org-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The harbor and rivers of Hampton Roads were immediately recognised as prime locations for commerce, shipbuilding and military installations, with the fortifications at\n       <a href="/wiki/Old_Point_Comfort" title="Old Point Comfort">\n        Old Point Comfort\n       </a>\n       established as early as 1610, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Naval_Shipyard" title="Norfolk Naval Shipyard">\n        Gosport Navy Yard\n       </a>\n       (later Norfolk Naval Shipyard) in 1767. The decisive battle of the Revolution was won at\n       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown" title="Siege of Yorktown">\n        Yorktown\n       </a>\n       in 1781, and the first naval action of the\n       <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">\n        War of 1812\n       </a>\n       took place in Hampton Roads, when a\n       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">\n        Royal Naval\n       </a>\n       vessel was seized by the American privateer\n       <i>\n        Dash\n       </i>\n       . Later the entrance from Chesapeake Bay was equipped with new fortifications (\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Monroe" title="Fort Monroe">\n        Fort Monroe\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Wool" title="Fort Wool">\n        Fort Wool\n       </a>\n       ), much of the building work being supervised by a young military engineer\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">\n        Robert E. Lee\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the American Civil War (1861\xe2\x80\x931865), the historic\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hampton_Roads" title="Battle of Hampton Roads">\n        Battle of Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n       between the first American\n       <a href="/wiki/Ironclad_warship" title="Ironclad warship">\n        ironclad warships\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/USS_Monitor" title="USS Monitor">\n        USS\n        <i>\n         Monitor\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/CSS_Virginia" title="CSS Virginia">\n        CSS\n        <i>\n         Virginia\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       , took place off\n       <a href="/wiki/Sewell%27s_Point" title="Sewell\'s Point">\n        Sewell\'s Point\n       </a>\n       in 1862. The battle was inconclusive, but Union forces later took control of Hampton Roads, Norfolk, and the lower James River, though they were thwarted from venturing further upstream by a strong Confederate battery at\n       <a href="/wiki/Drewry%27s_Bluff" title="Drewry\'s Bluff">\n        Drewry\'s Bluff\n       </a>\n       . Also in 1862, Fort Monroe was the launching place for Union General\n       <a href="/wiki/George_B._McClellan" title="George B. McClellan">\n        George McClellan\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Peninsula_Campaign" title="Peninsula Campaign">\n        massive advance\n       </a>\n       up the Virginia Peninsula, which almost reached the Confederate capital\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">\n        Richmond\n       </a>\n       , before the\n       <a href="/wiki/Seven_Days_Battles" title="Seven Days Battles">\n        Seven Days Battles\n       </a>\n       forced him back. In 1865, as the Confederacy was near collapse, President Abraham Lincoln met with three senior Confederates at Hampton Roads in an\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads_Conference" title="Hampton Roads Conference">\n        unsuccessful bid\n       </a>\n       for a negotiated peace.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some former slaves had been\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Contraband_Camp" title="Grand Contraband Camp">\n        camped\n       </a>\n       near Fort Monroe, where they were declared to be\n       <a href="/wiki/Contraband_(American_Civil_War)" title="Contraband (American Civil War)">\n        Contraband of war\n       </a>\n       , instead of being returned to their former owners.\n       <a href="/wiki/Booker_T._Washington" title="Booker T. Washington">\n        Booker T. Washington\n       </a>\n       was among the freedmen who attended the local school, which evolved into the present-day\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_University" title="Hampton University">\n        Hampton University\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">\n        20th century\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 20th century">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamestown_Exposition" title="Jamestown Exposition">\n        Jamestown Exposition\n       </a>\n       for the 300th anniversary of the 1607 founding of\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">\n        Jamestown\n       </a>\n       was held at\n       <a href="/wiki/Sewell%27s_Point" title="Sewell\'s Point">\n        Sewell\'s Point\n       </a>\n       in a rural section of\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_County,_Virginia" title="Norfolk County, Virginia">\n        Norfolk County\n       </a>\n       in 1907.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       President\n       <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">\n        Theodore Roosevelt\n       </a>\n       arrived by water in the harbor of Hampton Roads, as did other notable persons such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Mark_Twain" title="Mark Twain">\n        Mark Twain\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_H._Rogers" title="Henry H. Rogers">\n        Henry Huttleston Rogers\n       </a>\n       , who both arrived aboard the latter\'s steam yacht\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Kanawha_(1899)" title="Kanawha (1899)">\n         Kanawha\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . A major naval display was featured, and the U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_White_Fleet" title="Great White Fleet">\n        Great White Fleet\n       </a>\n       made an appearance. The leaders of the U.S. Navy apparently did not fail to note the ideal harbor conditions, as was later proved.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Beginning in 1917, as the United States became involved in World War I under President\n       <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">\n        Woodrow Wilson\n       </a>\n       , formerly rural\n       <a href="/wiki/Sewell%27s_Point" title="Sewell\'s Point">\n        Sewell\'s Point\n       </a>\n       became the site of what grew to become the largest Naval Base in the world which was established by the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">\n        United States Navy\n       </a>\n       and is now known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Norfolk" title="Naval Station Norfolk">\n        Naval Station Norfolk\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Twice in the 20th century, inhabitants mostly African American were displaced when land along the northern side of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Peninsula" title="Virginia Peninsula">\n        Peninsula\n       </a>\n       primarily in\n       <a href="/wiki/York_County,_Virginia" title="York County, Virginia">\n        York County\n       </a>\n       west of Yorktown was taken in large tracts for military use during World War I and World War II, creating the present-day U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/Naval_Weapons_Station_Yorktown" title="Naval Weapons Station Yorktown">\n        Naval Weapons Station Yorktown\n       </a>\n       , which includes Cheatham Annex, and a former\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seabee_(US_Navy)" title="Seabee (US Navy)">\n        Seabee\n       </a>\n       base which became\n       <a href="/wiki/Camp_Peary" title="Camp Peary">\n        Camp Peary\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Communities including\n       <a href="/wiki/Lackey,_Virginia" title="Lackey, Virginia">\n        "the Reservation"\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Halstead%27s_Point,_Virginia" title="Halstead\'s Point, Virginia">\n        Halstead\'s Point\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Penniman,_Virginia" title="Penniman, Virginia">\n        Penniman\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bigler%27s_Mill,_Virginia" title="Bigler\'s Mill, Virginia">\n        Bigler\'s Mill\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Magruder,_Virginia" title="Magruder, Virginia">\n        Magruder\n       </a>\n       were all\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Former_counties,_cities,_and_towns_of_Virginia" title="Former counties, cities, and towns of Virginia">\n        lost\n       </a>\n       and absorbed into the large military bases.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although some left the area entirely, many of the displaced families chose to relocate nearby to\n       <a href="/wiki/Grove,_Virginia" title="Grove, Virginia">\n        Grove\n       </a>\n       , an unincorporated town in southeastern\n       <a href="/wiki/James_City_County,_Virginia" title="James City County, Virginia">\n        James City County\n       </a>\n       where many generations of some of those families now reside. From a population estimated at only 37 in 1895, Grove had grown to an estimated 1,100 families by the end of the 20th century. (To its north, Grove actually borders the Naval Weapons Station property and on its extreme east, a portion of the U.S. Army\'s land at\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Eustis" title="Fort Eustis">\n        Fort Eustis\n       </a>\n       extends across Skiffe\'s Creek, although there is no direct access to either base).\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_Williamsburg">\n        Colonial Williamsburg\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Colonial Williamsburg">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Williamsburg" title="Colonial Williamsburg">\n        Colonial Williamsburg\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       It was the dream of an Episcopal priest to save his 18th-century church building by turning Williamsburg into the world\'s largest\n       <a href="/wiki/Living_museum" title="Living museum">\n        living museum\n       </a>\n       . Wlliamsburg replaced Jamestown at the very end of the 17th century after a disastrous fire. It was the capital of the colony and the new State of Virginia from 1699 to 1780. The capital was moved to Richmond in 1780. Williamsburg became a "sleepy" small town. During the Civil War the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Williamsburg" title="Battle of Williamsburg">\n        Battle of Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       was fought nearby during the Peninsula Campaign in the Spring months of 1862.. The decaying town was not located along any major waterway and did not have railroad access until 1881. Perhaps due to the secure inland location originally known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Plantation_(Virginia)" title="Middle Plantation (Virginia)">\n        Middle Plantation\n       </a>\n       Williamsburg missed growth and economic expansion in the 19th century. The main economic engines were\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_College_of_William_%26_Mary" title="The College of William &amp; Mary">\n        The College of William &amp; Mary\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_State_Hospital_(Virginia)" title="Eastern State Hospital (Virginia)">\n        Eastern State Hospital\n       </a>\n       . The College of William and Mary was chartered by the Crown and is the only pre-Independence college to have kept it. In addition to the city\'s historic past, quite a few buildings of antiquity from the 18th century were still extant, although time was taking a toll by the early 20th century. The Reverend Dr.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/W.A.R._Goodwin" title="W.A.R. Goodwin">\n        W.A.R. Goodwin\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Bruton_Parish_Church" title="Bruton Parish Church">\n        Bruton Parish Church\n       </a>\n       motive was to only to save historic church building which was secured by 1907. He subsequently served in\n       <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">\n        Rochester, New York\n       </a>\n       for many years. Upon returning to Williamsburg in 1923 he realized that many of the other colonial-era buildings were deteriorating and their existence was at risk.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Goodwin dreamt of a much larger restoration of the colonial town. A cleric of modest means, he first sought support and financing from a number of sources before successfully drawing the interests before receiving major financial support from\n       <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">\n        Standard Oil\n       </a>\n       heir and philanthropist\n       <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller_Jr." title="John D. Rockefeller Jr.">\n        John D. Rockefeller Jr.\n       </a>\n       and his wife\n       <a href="/wiki/Abby_Aldrich_Rockefeller" title="Abby Aldrich Rockefeller">\n        Abby Aldrich Rockefeller\n       </a>\n       . The result is the creation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Williamsburg" title="Colonial Williamsburg">\n        Colonial Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       with extensive restoration of buildings such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Wren_Building" title="Wren Building">\n        Wren Building\n       </a>\n       of the College of William &amp; Mary and the Governor\'s Palace, and the transformation of downtown Williamsburg area into Historic District of restored buildings. Many 19th century buildings were removed.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By the 1930s, Colonial Williamsburg had become the centerpiece of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Historic_Triangle" title="Historic Triangle">\n        Historic Triangle\n       </a>\n       of Colonial Virginia. These were, of course, Jamestown, where the colony started, Williamsburg, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Yorktown,_Virginia" title="Yorktown, Virginia">\n        Yorktown\n       </a>\n       , where independence from\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">\n        Great Britain\n       </a>\n       was won. The three points were joined by the U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">\n        National Park Service\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Parkway" title="Colonial Parkway">\n        Colonial Parkway\n       </a>\n       , a remarkable accomplishment in course of 27 years. The Historic Triangle area of the Hampton Roads region became one of the largest tourist attractions in the entire world.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In Dr. Goodwin\'s words: "Williamsburg is Jamestown continued, and Yorktown is Williamsburg vindicated."\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Historic_Triangle" title="Historic Triangle">\n        Historic Triangle\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span id=\'Other_notable_Hampton_Roads_"firsts"\'>\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_notable_Hampton_Roads_.22firsts.22">\n        Other notable Hampton Roads "firsts"\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title=\'Edit section: Other notable Hampton Roads "firsts"\'>\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       America\'s first free public schools, the Syms and Eaton free schools (later combined as\n       <a href="/wiki/Syms-Eaton_Academy" title="Syms-Eaton Academy">\n        Syms-Eaton Academy\n       </a>\n       ), were established in Hampton in 1634 and 1659 respectively. The Syms-Eaton Academy was later renamed Hampton Academy and in 1852 became part of the public school system, thus\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hampton_High_School_(Hampton,_Virginia)" title="Hampton High School (Hampton, Virginia)">\n        Hampton High School\n       </a>\n       lays claim to being the oldest public school in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The trust fund created from the Syms and Eaton donations has remained intact since the 17th century and was incorporated into support for the Hampton public school system.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1957, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads_Bridge%E2%80%93Tunnel" title="Hampton Roads Bridge\xe2\x80\x93Tunnel">\n        Hampton Roads Bridge\xe2\x80\x93Tunnel\n       </a>\n       was the first\n       <a href="/wiki/Bridge%E2%80%93tunnel" title="Bridge\xe2\x80\x93tunnel">\n        bridge\xe2\x80\x93tunnel\n       </a>\n       complex in the world, to be followed by the area\'s much longer\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge%E2%80%93Tunnel" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge\xe2\x80\x93Tunnel">\n        Chesapeake Bay Bridge\xe2\x80\x93Tunnel\n       </a>\n       in 1963. This was followed by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Monitor%E2%80%93Merrimac_Memorial_Bridge%E2%80%93Tunnel" title="Monitor\xe2\x80\x93Merrimac Memorial Bridge\xe2\x80\x93Tunnel">\n        Monitor\xe2\x80\x93Merrimac Memorial Bridge\xe2\x80\x93Tunnel\n       </a>\n       in 1992. The prevalence of bridge\xe2\x80\x93tunnels in the area is due to the number of shipbuilding and naval bases in the area. Access to the open ocean from Norfolk Naval Shipyard (in Portsmouth), Naval Station Norfolk, Joint Expeditionary Base Little Creek \xe2\x80\x93 Fort Story, and Newport News Shipbuilding (where all U.S. nuclear aircraft carriers have been built) do not pass under any bridges. Passing under bridges was considered a potential threat to the U.S. fleet.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 1960s, the first\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">\n        astronauts\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Mercury" title="Project Mercury">\n        Project Mercury\n       </a>\n       trained at the\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       facility adjacent to Hampton\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Langley_Air_Force_Base" title="Langley Air Force Base">\n        Langley Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       . Local features including\n       <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Boulevard" title="Mercury Boulevard">\n        Mercury Boulevard\n       </a>\n       and a succession of astronaut-name bridges over the Hampton creek commemorate this fact.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._military">\n        U.S. military\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: U.S. military">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The military has a large presence in the region. Area military facilities (alphabetically) include:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Camp_Allen" title="Camp Allen">\n           Camp Allen\n          </a>\n          , in Norfolk\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Camp_Peary" title="Camp Peary">\n           Camp Peary\n          </a>\n          , in York County\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a class="external text" href="http://www.uscg.mil/d5/" rel="nofollow">\n           Coast Guard 5th District\n          </a>\n          , in Portsmouth\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a class="external text" href="http://www.dcms.uscg.mil/Our-Organization/Director-of-Operational-Logistics-DOL/Bases/Base-Portsmouth/" rel="nofollow">\n           Coast Guard Base Portsmouth\n          </a>\n          in Portsmouth\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Training_Center_Yorktown" title="Training Center Yorktown">\n           Coast Guard Training Center Yorktown\n          </a>\n          , in York County\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fleet_Training_Center_Dam_Neck" title="Fleet Training Center Dam Neck">\n           Fleet Training Center Dam Neck\n          </a>\n          , in Virginia Beach\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Fort_Eustis" title="Fort Eustis">\n           Fort Eustis\n          </a>\n          , in Newport News\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Fort_Monroe" title="Fort Monroe">\n           Fort Monroe\n          </a>\n          , in Hampton (closed in September 2011)\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joint_Expeditionary_Base_East" title="Joint Expeditionary Base East">\n           Joint Expeditionary Base East\n          </a>\n          , in Virginia Beach\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Lafayette River Complex (LRC), in Norfolk\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Langley_Air_Force_Base" title="Langley Air Force Base">\n           Langley Air Force Base\n          </a>\n          , in Hampton\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Oceana" title="Naval Air Station Oceana">\n           Naval Air Station Oceana\n          </a>\n          , in Virginia Beach\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Amphibious_Base_Little_Creek" title="Naval Amphibious Base Little Creek">\n           Naval Amphibious Base Little Creek\n          </a>\n          , in Virginia Beach\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Naval_Medical_Center_Portsmouth" title="Naval Medical Center Portsmouth">\n           Naval Medical Center Portsmouth\n          </a>\n          , in Portsmouth\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Norfolk" title="Naval Station Norfolk">\n           Naval Station Norfolk\n          </a>\n          , in Norfolk\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Naval_Support_Activity_Hampton_Roads" title="Naval Support Activity Hampton Roads">\n           Naval Support Activity Hampton Roads\n          </a>\n          , in Chesapeake\n          <ul>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Naval_Consolidated_Brig,_Chesapeake" title="Naval Consolidated Brig, Chesapeake">\n             Naval Consolidated Brig, Chesapeake\n            </a>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Naval Support Activity Northwest Annex, in Chesapeake\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Naval_Weapons_Station_Yorktown" title="Naval Weapons Station Yorktown">\n           Naval Weapons Station Yorktown\n          </a>\n          , in York County\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Naval_Shipyard" title="Norfolk Naval Shipyard">\n           Norfolk Naval Shipyard\n          </a>\n          , in Portsmouth (not to be confused with\n          <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Naval_Shipyard" title="Portsmouth Naval Shipyard">\n           Portsmouth Naval Shipyard\n          </a>\n          , in\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kittery" title="Kittery">\n           Kittery\n          </a>\n          ,\n          <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">\n           Maine\n          </a>\n          )\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/St._Julien%27s_Creek_Annex" title="St. Julien\'s Creek Annex">\n           Saint Julian\'s Creek Naval Depot Annex\n          </a>\n          , in Chesapeake\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">\n        Government\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Government">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The area consists of ten independent cities and seven counties. Each independent city has the powers and responsibilities of a county, including maintaining roads, courts, schools, and public safety. Some cities share these responsibilities with an adjoining county.\n       <a href="/wiki/Incorporated_town" title="Incorporated town">\n        Incorporated towns\n       </a>\n       located within counties in Virginia do not operate independently.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The localities come together to consult on regional issues. Virginia defines regional planning districts by law. District members are usually independent cities and counties. Localities around the state may belong to more than one Planning District, as their constituents may have interests which cross over individual planning district boundaries.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Hampton Roads Planning District Commission (HRPDC) currently includes 16 cities and counties in Virginia, and represents over 1.6\xc2\xa0million people.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The 16 jurisdictions include:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        the Cities of Chesapeake, Franklin, Hampton, Newport News, Norfolk, Poquoson, Portsmouth, Suffolk, Virginia Beach, and Williamsburg,\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        the Counties of Gloucester, Isle of Wight, James City, Southampton, Surry, and York\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       There are incorporated towns in three of the counties (Isle of Wight, Southampton and Surry) within the district.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The differences between the service area of the HRPDC and the federally defined metropolitan statistical area (MSA) are:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Southampton County and the City of Franklin are not in the MSA.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Mathews County is in the MSA but not the HRPDC.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The MSA includes Currituck County, North Carolina, but the HRPDC does not.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       The federal government has two major research laboratories in the area. NASA-Langley, on the northeast edge of Hampton near Poquoson, is the home of a variety of aeronautics research, including several one-of-a-kind wind tunnels. The Department of Energy\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson_National_Accelerator_Facility" title="Thomas Jefferson National Accelerator Facility">\n        Thomas Jefferson National Accelerator Facility\n       </a>\n       (known as \'Jefferson Lab\')\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       conducts cutting edge physics research in\n       <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">\n        Newport News\n       </a>\n       ; the lab hosts the Continuous Electron Beam Accelerator Facility (CEBAF)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and a kilowatt-class\n       <a href="/wiki/Free-electron_laser" title="Free-electron laser">\n        free-electron laser\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2100" data-file-width="1500" height="350" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg/250px-Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg/375px-Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg/500px-Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         View of the Elizabeth River with Downtown Norfolk at top right. The carrier in the foreground is\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_Harry_S._Truman_(CVN-75)" title="USS Harry S. Truman (CVN-75)">\n          USS\n          <i>\n           Harry S. Truman\n          </i>\n          (CVN-75)\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The water area known as Hampton Roads is a wide channel through which the waters of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_River_(Virginia)" title="James River (Virginia)">\n        James River\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nansemond_River" title="Nansemond River">\n        Nansemond River\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_River_(Virginia)" title="Elizabeth River (Virginia)">\n        Elizabeth River\n       </a>\n       pass (between\n       <a href="/wiki/Old_Point_Comfort" title="Old Point Comfort">\n        Old Point Comfort\n       </a>\n       to the north and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sewell%27s_Point" title="Sewell\'s Point">\n        Sewell\'s Point\n       </a>\n       to the south) into the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       and the Atlantic Ocean.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Norfolk and Hampton Roads are among the worst-hit parts of the United States regarding\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming" title="Effects of global warming">\n        effects of global warming\n       </a>\n       . As of 2016, the region is a few decades ahead in feeling the effects of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea-level_rise" title="Sea-level rise">\n        sea-level rise\n       </a>\n       compared to many American coastal areas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The geology and topography of the Hampton Roads region is influenced by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Impact_Crater" title="Chesapeake Bay Impact Crater">\n        Chesapeake Bay Impact Crater\n       </a>\n       which is one of three factors contributing to the sinking of Hampton Roads at a rate between 15 and 23 centimeters (5.9 and 9.1 inches) per century.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The region has extensive natural areas, including 26 miles (42\xc2\xa0km) of Atlantic Ocean and Chesapeake Bay beaches, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Dismal_Swamp" title="Great Dismal Swamp">\n        Great Dismal Swamp\n       </a>\n       , picturesque rivers, state parks, wildlife refuges, and botanical gardens. Inland from the bay, the region includes\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Drummond" title="Lake Drummond">\n        Lake Drummond\n       </a>\n       , one of only two natural lakes found in Virginia, and miles of waterfront property along the various rivers and waterways. The region\'s native flora is consistent with that of the Southeast Coastal Plain and the lower Southeast Maritime Forest.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        land area\n       </b>\n       which constitutes "Hampton Roads" varies depending upon perspective and purpose. Most of the land area of Hampton Roads is geographically divided into 2 smaller regions: the eastern portion of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Peninsula" title="Virginia Peninsula">\n        Virginia Peninsula\n       </a>\n       (the Peninsula) and\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Hampton_Roads" title="South Hampton Roads">\n        South Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n       (locally known as "the Southside"), which are separated by the harbor. When speaking of communities of Hampton Roads, virtually all sources (including the three discussed in the following paragraphs) include the seven major cities, two smaller ones, and three counties within those two subregions.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Peninsula" title="Middle Peninsula">\n        Middle Peninsula\n       </a>\n       counties of Gloucester and Mathews, while not part of the geographical Hampton Roads area, are included in the vast metropolitan region\'s population. Also, a small portion of northeastern North Carolina (\n       <a href="/wiki/Currituck_County,_North_Carolina" title="Currituck County, North Carolina">\n        Currituck County\n       </a>\n       ) is included in the region\'s statistics. Due to a peculiarity in the drawing of the Virginia-North Carolina border,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knott%27s_Island,_North_Carolina" title="Knott\'s Island, North Carolina">\n        Knott\'s Island\n       </a>\n       in that county is connected to Virginia by land, but is only accessible to other parts of North Carolina across waterways via a ferry system.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Each of the following current cities, counties and towns is included by at least one of the three organizations that define "Hampton Roads"\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Welcome_To_HamptonVA.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Welcome_To_HamptonVA.jpg/250px-Welcome_To_HamptonVA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Welcome_To_HamptonVA.jpg/375px-Welcome_To_HamptonVA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Welcome_To_HamptonVA.jpg/500px-Welcome_To_HamptonVA.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Welcome_To_HamptonVA.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Hampton is a Hampton Roads community.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Hampton Roads area consists of nine independent cities (which are not part of any county).\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake,_Virginia" title="Chesapeake, Virginia">\n        Chesapeake\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">\n        Norfolk\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">\n        Portsmouth\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Suffolk,_Virginia" title="Suffolk, Virginia">\n        Suffolk\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">\n        Virginia Beach\n       </a>\n       cover the Southside of Hampton Roads while\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Virginia" title="Hampton, Virginia">\n        Hampton\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">\n        Newport News\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Poquoson,_Virginia" title="Poquoson, Virginia">\n        Poquoson\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n        Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       reside on the Peninsula.\n       <a href="/wiki/Franklin,_Virginia" title="Franklin, Virginia">\n        Franklin\n       </a>\n       borders Suffolk but the Census Bureau does not consider it as a part of the metro area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whitehouse.gov_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-whitehouse.gov-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The metro area has one county in North Carolina,\n       <a href="/wiki/Currituck_County,_North_Carolina" title="Currituck County, North Carolina">\n        Currituck\n       </a>\n       . The remaining counties, in Virginia, include\n       <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight_County,_Virginia" title="Isle of Wight County, Virginia">\n        Isle of Wight\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Surry_County,_Virginia" title="Surry County, Virginia">\n        Surry\n       </a>\n       on the Southside,\n       <a href="/wiki/James_City_County,_Virginia" title="James City County, Virginia">\n        James City\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/York_County,_Virginia" title="York County, Virginia">\n        York\n       </a>\n       on the Virginia Peninsula, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_County,_Virginia" title="Gloucester County, Virginia">\n        Gloucester\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mathews_County,_Virginia" title="Mathews County, Virginia">\n        Mathews\n       </a>\n       on the Middle Peninsula. While\n       <a href="/wiki/Southampton_County,_Virginia" title="Southampton County, Virginia">\n        Southampton\n       </a>\n       is adjacent to Surry, Isle of Wight, and the City of Suffolk, the Census Bureau does not consider it part of the metro area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whitehouse.gov_31-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-whitehouse.gov-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Five\n       <a href="/wiki/Incorporated_town" title="Incorporated town">\n        incorporated towns\n       </a>\n       reside in the metro area including\n       <a href="/wiki/Claremont,_Virginia" title="Claremont, Virginia">\n        Claremont\n       </a>\n       in Surry County,\n       <a href="/wiki/Dendron,_Virginia" title="Dendron, Virginia">\n        Dendron\n       </a>\n       in Surry County,\n       <a href="/wiki/Smithfield,_Virginia" title="Smithfield, Virginia">\n        Smithfield\n       </a>\n       in Isle of Wight County,\n       <a href="/wiki/Surry,_Virginia" title="Surry, Virginia">\n        Surry\n       </a>\n       , Surry County\'s seat, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Virginia" title="Windsor, Virginia">\n        Windsor\n       </a>\n       in Isle of Wight County. (Two other incorporated towns,\n       <a href="/wiki/Boykins,_Virginia" title="Boykins, Virginia">\n        Boykins\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Courtland,_Virginia" title="Courtland, Virginia">\n        Courtland\n       </a>\n       are located in Southampton County, and therefore, like the county within which they are located, are not part of the federally defined metropolitan area).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whitehouse.gov_31-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-whitehouse.gov-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other unincorporated towns and communities in the metropolitan area which are not within its cities include\n       <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Courthouse,_Virginia" title="Gloucester Courthouse, Virginia">\n        Gloucester Courthouse\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Point,_Virginia" title="Gloucester Point, Virginia">\n        Gloucester Point\n       </a>\n       in Gloucester County,\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Wight_Courthouse,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Isle of Wight Courthouse, Virginia (page does not exist)">\n        Isle of Wight Courthouse\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rushmere,_Virginia" title="Rushmere, Virginia">\n        Rushmere\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rescue,_Virginia" title="Rescue, Virginia">\n        Rescue\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Carrollton,_Virginia" title="Carrollton, Virginia">\n        Carrollton\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Benns_Church,_Virginia" title="Benns Church, Virginia">\n        Benns Church\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Walters,_Virginia" title="Walters, Virginia">\n        Walters\n       </a>\n       in Isle of Wight County,\n       <a href="/wiki/Yorktown,_Virginia" title="Yorktown, Virginia">\n        Yorktown\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Grafton,_Virginia" title="Grafton, Virginia">\n        Grafton\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Seaford,_Virginia" title="Seaford, Virginia">\n        Seaford\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tabb,_Virginia" title="Tabb, Virginia">\n        Tabb\n       </a>\n       in York County,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">\n        Jamestown\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ford%27s_Colony,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ford\'s Colony, Virginia (page does not exist)">\n        Ford\'s Colony\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Grove,_Virginia" title="Grove, Virginia">\n        Grove\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightfoot,_Virginia" title="Lightfoot, Virginia">\n        Lightfoot\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Toano,_Virginia" title="Toano, Virginia">\n        Toano\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Norge,_Virginia" title="Norge, Virginia">\n        Norge\n       </a>\n       in James City County,\n       <a href="/wiki/Moyock,_North_Carolina" title="Moyock, North Carolina">\n        Moyock\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Knotts_Island,_North_Carolina" title="Knotts Island, North Carolina">\n        Knotts Island\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Currituck,_North_Carolina" title="Currituck, North Carolina">\n        Currituck\n       </a>\n       in Currituck County, North Carolina.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whitehouse.gov_31-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-whitehouse.gov-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Hampton Roads MSA, with a population of about 1.7\xc2\xa0million, is the seventh largest metropolitan area in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">\n        Southeastern United States\n       </a>\n       after\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_metropolitan_area" title="Washington metropolitan area">\n        Washington metropolitan area\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Florida_metropolitan_area" title="South Florida metropolitan area">\n        Miami\xe2\x80\x93Fort Lauderdale\xe2\x80\x93Pompano Beach, FL MSA\n       </a>\n
