 ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_metropolitan_area" title="Atlanta metropolitan area">\n        Atlanta\xe2\x80\x93Sandy Springs\xe2\x80\x93Marietta, GA MSA\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Area" title="Tampa Bay Area">\n        Tampa\xe2\x80\x93St. Petersburg\xe2\x80\x93Clearwater, FL MSA\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Orlando" title="Greater Orlando">\n        Orlando\xe2\x80\x93Kissimmee, FL MSA\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_metropolitan_area" title="Charlotte metropolitan area">\n        Charlotte\xe2\x80\x93Gastonia-Rock Hill, NC\xe2\x80\x93SC MSA\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">\n        Demographics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n        2010 Census\n       </a>\n       , the overall racial composition of Hampton Roads was as follows:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-United_States_Census_Bureau_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-United_States_Census_Bureau-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">\n         White or Caucasian\n        </a>\n        : 59.6%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">\n         Black or African American\n        </a>\n        : 31.3%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">\n         American Indian\n        </a>\n        : 0.4%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">\n         Asian\n        </a>\n        : 3.5%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Some other race: 1.7%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">\n         Two or more races\n        </a>\n        : 3.4%\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       In addition, 5.4% of the population were\n       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">\n        Hispanic or Latino\n       </a>\n       (of any race). 57.2% of the population were of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites" title="Non-Hispanic Whites">\n        non-Hispanic White\n       </a>\n       background.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">\n        Transportation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transportation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Hampton_Roads" title="Transportation in Hampton Roads">\n        Transportation in Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PortsmouthNorfolkFerry1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/PortsmouthNorfolkFerry1.jpg/200px-PortsmouthNorfolkFerry1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/PortsmouthNorfolkFerry1.jpg/300px-PortsmouthNorfolkFerry1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/PortsmouthNorfolkFerry1.jpg/400px-PortsmouthNorfolkFerry1.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PortsmouthNorfolkFerry1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Ferry between Norfolk and Portsmouth\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Historically, from the earliest times, the harbor was the key to the Hampton Roads area\'s growth, both on land and in water-related activities and events. Ironically, the harbor and its tributary waterways were (and still are) both important transportation conduits and obstacles to other land-based commerce and travel. Yet, the community leaders learned to overcome them.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In modern times, the region has faced increasing transportation challenges as it has become largely urbanized, with additional traffic needs. In the 21st century, the conflicts between traffic on vital waterways and land-based travel continue to present the area\'s leaders with extraordinary transportation challenges, both for additional capacity, and as the existing infrastructure, much of it originally built with\n       <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">\n        toll revenues\n       </a>\n       , has aged without an adequate source of funding to repair or build replacements. The now-closed\n       <a href="/wiki/Kings_Highway_Bridge" title="Kings Highway Bridge">\n        Kings Highway Bridge\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Suffolk,_Virginia" title="Suffolk, Virginia">\n        Suffolk\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Bridge" title="Jordan Bridge">\n        Jordan Bridge\n       </a>\n       closed by neighboring\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake,_Virginia" title="Chesapeake, Virginia">\n        Chesapeake\n       </a>\n       in 2008 were each built in the 1920s. These were considered locally prime examples of this situation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2007, the new\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads_Transportation_Authority" title="Hampton Roads Transportation Authority">\n        Hampton Roads Transportation Authority\n       </a>\n       (HRTA) was formed under a controversial state law to levy various additional taxes to generate funding for major regional transportation projects, including a long-sought and costly additional crossing of the harbor of Hampton Roads (The Hampton Roads Bridge Tunnel, Monitor-Merrimac Bridge Tunnel, and the James River Bridge are the existing crossings). As of March 2008, although its projects were considered to be needed, the agency\'s future was in some question while its controversial sources of funding were being reconsidered in light of a Virginia Supreme Court decision.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TugboatNorfolkVA.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/TugboatNorfolkVA.jpg/200px-TugboatNorfolkVA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/TugboatNorfolkVA.jpg/300px-TugboatNorfolkVA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/TugboatNorfolkVA.jpg/400px-TugboatNorfolkVA.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TugboatNorfolkVA.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A tugboat in Norfolk\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Newport_News/Williamsburg_International_Airport" title="Newport News/Williamsburg International Airport">\n        Newport News/Williamsburg International Airport\n       </a>\n       , located in Newport News, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_International_Airport" title="Norfolk International Airport">\n        Norfolk International Airport\n       </a>\n       , in Norfolk, both cater to passengers from Hampton Roads. The primary airport for the Virginia Peninsula is the Newport News/Williamsburg International Airport. The Airport experienced a 4th year of record, double-digit growth through 2011, making it one of the fastest growing airports in the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newport_News.2FWilliamsburg_International_Airport_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Newport_News.2FWilliamsburg_International_Airport-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2012 however, the airport lost its biggest carrier and has seen massive declines in passenger service, culminating in layoffs of police officers and many other staff.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_International_Airport" title="Norfolk International Airport">\n        Norfolk International Airport\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">\n        IATA\n       </a>\n       :\n       <b>\n        ORF\n       </b>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">\n        ICAO\n       </a>\n       :\n       <b>\n        KORF\n       </b>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">\n        FAA\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">\n        LID\n       </a>\n       :\n       <b>\n        ORF\n       </b>\n       ), serves the region. The airport is located near Chesapeake Bay, along the city limits of\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">\n        Norfolk\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">\n        Virginia Beach\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ORF_History_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ORF_History-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Seven airlines provide nonstop services to twenty five destinations. ORF had 3,703,664 passengers take off or land at its facility and 68,778,934 pounds of cargo were processed through its facilities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ORF_Statistics_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ORF_Statistics-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads_Executive_Airport" title="Hampton Roads Executive Airport">\n        Hampton Roads Executive Airport\n       </a>\n       (KPVG), located on US460/US58, is the state\'s 3rd busiest General Aviation airport and hosts the largest number of general aviation aircraft of any Virginia airport. The airport offers flight training, avionics services, as well as major and minor airframe and powerplant repairs. There is also a sit-down restaurant in the terminal.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Regional_Airport" title="Chesapeake Regional Airport">\n        Chesapeake Regional Airport\n       </a>\n       (KCPK) provides similar general aviation services and is located in the city of Chesapeake. Additionally, many local general aviation pilots fly from the nearby Suffolk (KSFQ), Wakefield (KAKQ) and Franklin (KFKN) airports.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">\n        Amtrak\n       </a>\n       serves the region with\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Regional" title="Northeast Regional">\n        Northeast Regional\n       </a>\n       trains to its\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norfolk_(Amtrak_station)" title="Norfolk (Amtrak station)">\n        Norfolk\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Williamsburg_(Amtrak_station)" title="Williamsburg (Amtrak station)">\n        Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newport_News_(Amtrak_station)" title="Newport News (Amtrak station)">\n        Newport News\n       </a>\n       stations. The lines run west to\n       <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">\n        Richmond\n       </a>\n       then north to\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">\n        Washington, D.C.\n       </a>\n       and major cities north to\n       <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">\n        Boston\n       </a>\n       . Connecting buses are available between the Norfolk and Newport News stations and from both stations to Virginia Beach. A high-speed rail connection at Richmond to both the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">\n        Northeast Corridor\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southeast_High_Speed_Rail_Corridor" title="Southeast High Speed Rail Corridor">\n        Southeast High Speed Rail Corridor\n       </a>\n       are also under study.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SEHSR_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SEHSR-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intercity_bus" title="Intercity bus">\n        Intercity bus\n       </a>\n       service is provided by\n       <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Lines" title="Greyhound Lines">\n        Greyhound Lines\n       </a>\n       (Carolina Trailways) with bus stations in Newport News, Hampton, and Norfolk.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Transportation within Hampton Roads is served by a regional bus service,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads_Transit" title="Hampton Roads Transit">\n        Hampton Roads Transit\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Local routes serving Williamsburg, James City County, and upper York County is operated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg_Area_Transit_Authority" title="Williamsburg Area Transit Authority">\n        Williamsburg Area Transit Authority\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">\n        light rail\n       </a>\n       service known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Tide_Light_Rail" title="Tide Light Rail">\n        The Tide\n       </a>\n       was constructed in Norfolk. It began service in August 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Operated by Hampton Roads Transit, it is the first light rail service in the state. It is projected to have a daily ridership of between 7,130 and 11,400 passengers a day.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-September30_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-September30-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There has also been a light rail study in the Hampton \xe2\x80\x93 Newport News areas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRTP_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PRTP-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the 2016 election, a referendum was on the ballot in Virginia Beach to kill the planned, and mainly state-funded extension of the Tide to the commercial center of Virginia Beach and ultimately to the oceanfront. The ballot initiative won, cancelling the project. The transit authority and the state were left with new light rail cars and major infrastructure for the extension to be disposed of. There are no further plans for light rail mass transit initiatives within Virginia Beach.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:I-64_sign,_Hampton_Roads.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="664" data-file-width="346" height="422" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/I-64_sign%2C_Hampton_Roads.jpg/220px-I-64_sign%2C_Hampton_Roads.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/I-64_sign%2C_Hampton_Roads.jpg/330px-I-64_sign%2C_Hampton_Roads.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/I-64_sign%2C_Hampton_Roads.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:I-64_sign,_Hampton_Roads.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         I-64 on the Hampton Roads Beltway, north of I-264\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Hampton Roads area has an extensive network of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway" title="Interstate Highway">\n        Interstate Highways\n       </a>\n       , including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_64" title="Interstate 64">\n        Interstate 64\n       </a>\n       , the major east-west route to and from the area, and its spurs and bypasses of\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_264_(Virginia)" title="Interstate 264 (Virginia)">\n        I-264\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_464" title="Interstate 464">\n        I-464\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_564" title="Interstate 564">\n        I-564\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_664" title="Interstate 664">\n        I-664\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads_Beltway" title="Hampton Roads Beltway">\n        Hampton Roads Beltway\n       </a>\n       extends 56 miles (90\xc2\xa0km) on a long loop through the region, crossing the harbor on two toll-free\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bridge-tunnel" title="Bridge-tunnel">\n        bridge-tunnel\n       </a>\n       facilities. These crossings are the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads_Bridge-Tunnel" title="Hampton Roads Bridge-Tunnel">\n        Hampton Roads Bridge-Tunnel\n       </a>\n       between\n       <a href="/wiki/Phoebus,_Virginia" title="Phoebus, Virginia">\n        Phoebus\n       </a>\n       in Hampton and\n       <a href="/wiki/Willoughby_Spit" title="Willoughby Spit">\n        Willoughby Spit\n       </a>\n       in Norfolk and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monitor-Merrimac_Memorial_Bridge-Tunnel" title="Monitor-Merrimac Memorial Bridge-Tunnel">\n        Monitor-Merrimac Memorial Bridge-Tunnel\n       </a>\n       between Newport News and Suffolk. The Beltway connects with another Interstate highway and three arterial U.S. Highways at\n       <a href="/wiki/Bower%27s_Hill,_Virginia" title="Bower\'s Hill, Virginia">\n        Bower\'s Hill\n       </a>\n       near the northeastern edge of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Dismal_Swamp" title="Great Dismal Swamp">\n        Great Dismal Swamp\n       </a>\n       . Other major east-west routes are\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_58_(Virginia)" title="U.S. Route 58 (Virginia)">\n        U.S. Route 58\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_60_in_Virginia" title="U.S. Route 60 in Virginia">\n        U.S. Route 60\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_460_(Virginia)" title="U.S. Route 460 (Virginia)">\n        U.S. Route 460\n       </a>\n       . The major north-south routes are\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_13_(Virginia)" title="U.S. Route 13 (Virginia)">\n        U.S. Route 13\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_17_(Virginia)" title="U.S. Route 17 (Virginia)">\n        U.S. Route 17\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are also two other tunnels in the area, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Tunnel_(Virginia)" title="Midtown Tunnel (Virginia)">\n        Midtown Tunnel\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Tunnel" title="Downtown Tunnel">\n        Downtown Tunnel\n       </a>\n       joining Portsmouth and Norfolk, as well as the 17-mile (27\xc2\xa0km)-long\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge-Tunnel" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge-Tunnel">\n        Chesapeake Bay Bridge-Tunnel\n       </a>\n       , a toll facility which links the region with Virginia\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Virginia" title="Eastern Shore of Virginia">\n        Eastern Shore\n       </a>\n       which carries\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_13_(Virginia)" title="U.S. Route 13 (Virginia)">\n        US 13\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-facts-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The original Downtown Tunnel in conjunction with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Berkley_Bridge_(Virginia)" title="Berkley Bridge (Virginia)">\n        Berkley Bridge\n       </a>\n       were considered a single bridge and tunnel complex when completed in 1952, perhaps stimulating the innovative\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bridge-tunnel" title="Bridge-tunnel">\n        bridge-tunnel\n       </a>\n       design using\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Man-made_island" title="Man-made island">\n        man-made islands\n       </a>\n       when the Hampton Roads Bridge-Tunnel was planned, first opening in 1957. The\n       <a href="/wiki/George_P._Coleman_Memorial_Bridge" title="George P. Coleman Memorial Bridge">\n        George P. Coleman Memorial Bridge\n       </a>\n       is a major\n       <a href="/wiki/Toll_bridge" title="Toll bridge">\n        toll bridge\n       </a>\n       connecting U.S. Highway 17 on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Peninsula" title="Virginia Peninsula">\n        Peninsula\n       </a>\n       at\n       <a href="/wiki/Yorktown,_Virginia" title="Yorktown, Virginia">\n        Yorktown\n       </a>\n       with Virginia\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Peninsula" title="Middle Peninsula">\n        Middle Peninsula\n       </a>\n       region. Another major crossing of waterways is the\n       <a href="/wiki/James_River_Bridge" title="James River Bridge">\n        James River Bridge\n       </a>\n       , carrying\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_17" title="U.S. Highway 17">\n        US 17\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_258" title="U.S. Highway 258">\n        US 258\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Route_32_(Virginia)" title="Route 32 (Virginia)">\n        SR 32\n       </a>\n       from Newport News to\n       <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight_County,_Virginia" title="Isle of Wight County, Virginia">\n        Isle of Wight County\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bridges_and_Tunnels_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bridges_and_Tunnels-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The region is notable in that it has 2 types of public transport services via\n       <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">\n        ferries\n       </a>\n       . A passenger ferry is operated on the Elizabeth River between downtown areas of Norfolk and Portsmouth by HRT.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ferry_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ferry-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamestown_Ferry" title="Jamestown Ferry">\n        Jamestown Ferry\n       </a>\n       (also known as the Jamestown-Scotland Ferry) is an automobile ferry system on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_River_(Virginia)" title="James River (Virginia)">\n        James River\n       </a>\n       connecting\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">\n        Jamestown\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/James_City_County,_Virginia" title="James City County, Virginia">\n        James City County\n       </a>\n       with Scotland in\n       <a href="/wiki/Surry_County,_Virginia" title="Surry County, Virginia">\n        Surry County\n       </a>\n       . It carries\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Route_31_(Virginia)" title="State Route 31 (Virginia)">\n        State Route 31\n       </a>\n       . Operated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Department_of_Transportation" title="Virginia Department of Transportation">\n        VDOT\n       </a>\n       , it is the only 24-hour state-run ferry operation in Virginia and has over 90 employees. It operates four ferryboats, the\n       <i>\n        Pocahontas\n       </i>\n       , the\n       <i>\n        Williamsburg\n       </i>\n       , the\n       <i>\n        Surry\n       </i>\n       , and the\n       <i>\n        Virginia\n       </i>\n       . The facility is toll-free.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jamestown-Scotland_Ferry_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Jamestown-Scotland_Ferry-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">\n        Education\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Hampton Roads\' individual cities and counties administer their own K-12 education for their localities. In addition to public education, area residents have many private and religious school options.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The area also has a number of higher education options for area residents. Some offer only associates and technical degrees and certificates, while others award advanced degrees, including doctorates. Some are publicly funded, but the region also has a number of private and for-profit colleges. Additionally, a number of universities have established satellite campuses in the region.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_universities">\n        Public universities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Public universities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_Dominion_University_seal.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="316" data-file-width="315" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Old_Dominion_University_seal.png/150px-Old_Dominion_University_seal.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Old_Dominion_University_seal.png/225px-Old_Dominion_University_seal.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Old_Dominion_University_seal.png/300px-Old_Dominion_University_seal.png 2x" width="150"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_Dominion_University_seal.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Old Dominion University Seal\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/College_of_William_and_Mary" title="College of William and Mary">\n        College of William and Mary\n       </a>\n       in Williamsburg was founded in 1693 and has served as the second oldest institution of higher education in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Old_Dominion_University" title="Old Dominion University">\n        Old Dominion University\n       </a>\n       , founded as the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/College_of_William_and_Mary" title="College of William and Mary">\n        Norfolk Division of the College of William and Mary\n       </a>\n       in 1930, became an independent institution in 1962 and now offers degrees in 68 undergraduate and 95 (60 masters/35 doctoral) graduate degree programs. Norfolk\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Virginia_Medical_School" title="Eastern Virginia Medical School">\n        Eastern Virginia Medical School\n       </a>\n       , founded as a community medical school by the surrounding jurisdictions in 1973, is noted for its research into reproductive medicine\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-About_Jones_Institute_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-About_Jones_Institute-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and is located in the region\'s major medical complex in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghent_district" title="Ghent district">\n        Ghent district\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_State_University" title="Norfolk State University">\n        Norfolk State University\n       </a>\n       is the largest majority black university in Virginia and offers degrees in a wide variety of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" title="Liberal arts">\n        liberal arts\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AboutNSU_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AboutNSU-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Newport_University" title="Christopher Newport University">\n        Christopher Newport University\n       </a>\n       serves as a public university and is located in Newport News.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Private_universities">\n        Private universities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Private universities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Regent_University" title="Regent University">\n        Regent University\n       </a>\n       , a private university founded by Christian evangelist, television host and leader\n       <a href="/wiki/Pat_Robertson" title="Pat Robertson">\n        Pat Robertson\n       </a>\n       , has historically focused on graduate education but is attempting to establish an undergraduate program as well.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Regent_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Regent-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_University" title="Atlantic University">\n        Atlantic University\n       </a>\n       , associated with the Edgar Cayce organization\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Research_and_Enlightenment" title="Association for Research and Enlightenment">\n        Association for Research and Enlightenment\n       </a>\n       (ARE), offers instruction in New Age subjects and an M.A. in Transpersonal Studies.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-About_AU_56-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-About_AU-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Wesleyan_College" title="Virginia Wesleyan College">\n        Virginia Wesleyan College\n       </a>\n       is a small private\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" title="Liberal arts">\n        liberal arts\n       </a>\n       college on the border of Norfolk and Virginia Beach.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-About_VWU_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-About_VWU-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_University" title="Hampton University">\n        Hampton University\n       </a>\n       , a private\n       <a href="/wiki/Historically_black_colleges_and_universities" title="Historically black colleges and universities">\n        HBCU\n       </a>\n       university, has a long history serving Hampton.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Universities_with_satellite_campuses">\n        Universities with satellite campuses\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Universities with satellite campuses">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Several universities based outside Hampton Roads offer a limited selection of classes in the area.\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Tech" title="Virginia Tech">\n        Virginia Tech\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">\n        University of Virginia\n       </a>\n       have established a joint teaching center in Newport News.\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_University" title="George Washington University">\n        George Washington University\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Averett_University" title="Averett University">\n        Averett University\n       </a>\n       also maintain campuses there.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Troy_State_University" title="Troy State University">\n        Troy State University\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_International_University" title="Florida International University">\n        Florida International University\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Leo_University" title="Saint Leo University">\n        Saint Leo University\n       </a>\n       offer classes, primarily connected to one or more of the area\'s military bases.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="University_consortia">\n        University consortia\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: University consortia">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Aerospace" title="National Institute of Aerospace">\n        National Institute of Aerospace\n       </a>\n       (NIA) is a consortium of member universities:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgia_Tech" title="Georgia Tech">\n        Georgia Tech\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_University" title="Hampton University">\n        Hampton University\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Carolina_A%26T" title="North Carolina A&amp;T">\n        North Carolina A&amp;T\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Carolina_State" title="North Carolina State">\n        North Carolina State\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Old_Dominion_University" title="Old Dominion University">\n        Old Dominion University\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">\n        University of Virginia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Tech" title="Virginia Tech">\n        Virginia Tech\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/College_of_William_and_Mary" title="College of William and Mary">\n        College of William and Mary\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Newport_University" title="Christopher Newport University">\n        Christopher Newport University\n       </a>\n       . Their unique approach allows students pursuing M.S. and Ph.D. degrees the opportunity to take classes from any member university taught at the Institute.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Technical_education">\n        Technical education\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Technical education">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crimdell.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Crimdell.jpg/220px-Crimdell.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Crimdell.jpg/330px-Crimdell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Crimdell.jpg/440px-Crimdell.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crimdell.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Crim Dell in the heart of William &amp; Mary\'s wooded campus\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Area residents also have options for training for technical professions.\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Apprentice_School" title="The Apprentice School">\n        The Apprentice School\n       </a>\n       was founded in 1919 and offers four/five-year programs in mechanical and technical fields associated with the shipbuilding industry. Graduates from the Apprentice School go on to work at the Newport News Shipbuilding.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apprentice_School_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Apprentice_School-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Technology-focused\n       <a href="/wiki/ECPI_University" title="ECPI University">\n        ECPI University\n       </a>\n       has campuses in Virginia Beach and Newport News\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-About_ECPI_60-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-About_ECPI-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       while\n       <a href="/wiki/ITT_Technical_Institute" title="ITT Technical Institute">\n        ITT Technical Institute\n       </a>\n       has a campus in Norfolk.\n       <a href="/wiki/Bryant_%26_Stratton_College" title="Bryant &amp; Stratton College">\n        Bryant &amp; Stratton College\n       </a>\n       has campuses in\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach_Town_Center" title="Virginia Beach Town Center">\n        Virginia Beach Town Center\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Peninsula_Town_Center" title="Peninsula Town Center">\n        Peninsula Town Center\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Culinary Institute of Virginia\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is located in Norfolk.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Art_Institute_of_Virginia_Beach" title="The Art Institute of Virginia Beach">\n        The Art Institute of Virginia Beach\n       </a>\n       offers programs in the media arts, design and culinary arts fields.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Two-year_colleges">\n        Two-year colleges\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Two-year colleges">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Three institutions in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Community_College_System" title="Virginia Community College System">\n        Virginia Community College System\n       </a>\n       offer affordable higher education options for area residents.\n       <a href="/wiki/Tidewater_Community_College" title="Tidewater Community College">\n        Tidewater Community College\n       </a>\n       in Norfolk, Virginia Beach, Chesapeake, and Portsmouth,\n       <a href="/wiki/Paul_D._Camp_Community_College" title="Paul D. Camp Community College">\n        Paul D. Camp Community College\n       </a>\n       in Suffolk, Franklin, and Smithfield, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Nelson_Community_College" title="Thomas Nelson Community College">\n        Thomas Nelson Community College\n       </a>\n       in Hampton and Williamsburg offer two-year degrees and specialized training programs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCC_63-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TCC-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_education">\n        Religious education\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Religious education">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Bible training schools include Hampton University and Regent University, but also Canaan Theological College &amp; Seminary, Bethel College and Victory Baptist Bible College and Seminary in Hampton, Tabernacle Baptist Bible College &amp; Theological Seminary, Central Baptist Theological Seminary in Virginia Beach, Providence Bible College &amp; Theological Seminary in Norfolk and the Hampton Roads campus of the\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Leland_Center_for_Theological_Studies" title="John Leland Center for Theological Studies">\n        John Leland Center for Theological Studies\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Economy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Hampton Roads is home to four Fortune 500 companies. Representing the food industry, transportation, retail and shipbuilding, these four companies are located in\n       <a href="/wiki/Smithfield,_Virginia" title="Smithfield, Virginia">\n        Smithfield\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">\n        Norfolk\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake,_Virginia" title="Chesapeake, Virginia">\n        Chesapeake\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newport_News" title="Newport News">\n        Newport News\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div>\n       <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style=\'"border-collapse:\'>\n        <tr>\n         <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n          <dl>\n           <dt>\n            2013\n            <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">\n             Fortune 500\n            </a>\n            Corporations\n            <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n             <a href="#cite_note-65">\n              [65]\n             </a>\n            </sup>\n           </dt>\n          </dl>\n          <ul>\n           <li>\n            213\n            <a href="/wiki/Smithfield_Foods" title="Smithfield Foods">\n             Smithfield Foods\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            247\n            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern" title="Norfolk Southern">\n             Norfolk Southern\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            346\n            <a href="/wiki/Dollar_Tree" title="Dollar Tree">\n             Dollar Tree\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            380\n            <a href="/wiki/Huntington_Ingalls_Industries" title="Huntington Ingalls Industries">\n             Huntington Ingalls Industries\n            </a>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n          <div class="thumb tright">\n           <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n            <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hampton_roads_from_space.jpg">\n             <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="514" data-file-width="649" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Hampton_roads_from_space.jpg/200px-Hampton_roads_from_space.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Hampton_roads_from_space.jpg/300px-Hampton_roads_from_space.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Hampton_roads_from_space.jpg/400px-Hampton_roads_from_space.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n            </a>\n            <div class="thumbcaption">\n             <div class="magnify">\n              <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hampton_roads_from_space.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n              </a>\n             </div>\n             Hampton Roads from space\n            </div>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n          <p>\n           Hampton Roads has become known as the "world\'s greatest natural harbor". The port is located only 18 miles (29\xc2\xa0km) from open ocean on one of the world\'s deepest, natural ice-free harbors. Since 1989, Hampton Roads has been the mid-Atlantic leader in U.S. waterborne foreign commerce and is ranked second nationally behind the Port of South Louisiana based on export tonnage. When import and export tonnage are combined, the Port of Hampton Roads ranks as the third largest port in the country (following the ports of New Orleans/South Louisiana and Houston). In 1996, Hampton Roads was ranked ninth among major U.S. ports in vessel port calls with approximately 2,700. In addition, this port is the U.S. leader in coal exports. The coal loading facilities in the Port of Hampton Roads are able to load in excess of 65 million tons annually, giving the port the largest, most efficient and modern coal loading facilities in the world.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           It is little surprise therefore that the Hampton Roads region\'s economic base is largely port-related, including shipbuilding, ship repair, naval installations, cargo transfer and storage, and manufacturing related to the processing of imports and exports. Associated with the ports\' military role are almost 50,000 federal civilian employees.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The harbor of Hampton Roads is an important highway of commerce, especially for the cities of\n           <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">\n            Norfolk\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">\n            Portsmouth\n           </a>\n           , and\n           <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">\n            Newport News\n           </a>\n           .\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           <a href="/wiki/Huntington_Ingalls_Industries" title="Huntington Ingalls Industries">\n            Huntington Ingalls Industries\n           </a>\n           (formerly Newport News Shipbuilding and Drydock Company), was created in 2008 as a spinoff of\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northrop_Grumman_Newport_News" title="Northrop Grumman Newport News">\n            Northrop Grumman Newport News\n           </a>\n           and is the world\'s largest\n           <a href="/wiki/Shipyard" title="Shipyard">\n            shipyard\n           </a>\n           . It is located a short distance up the\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_River_(Virginia)" title="James River (Virginia)">\n            James River\n           </a>\n           . In Portsmouth, a few miles up the Elizabeth River, the historic\n           <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Naval_Shipyard" title="Norfolk Naval Shipyard">\n            Norfolk Naval Shipyard\n           </a>\n           is located. BAE Systems, formerly known as NORSHIPCO, operates from sites in the City of Norfolk. There are also several smaller shipyards, numerous docks and terminals.\n          </p>\n          <div class="thumb tright">\n           <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n            <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Northrop_Grumman_Newport_News_032007_015.png">\n             <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="522" data-file-width="800" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Northrop_Grumman_Newport_News_032007_015.png/200px-Northrop_Grumman_Newport_News_032007_015.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Northrop_Grumman_Newport_News_032007_015.png/300px-Northrop_Grumman_Newport_News_032007_015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Northrop_Grumman_Newport_News_032007_015.png/400px-Northrop_Grumman_Newport_News_032007_015.png 2x" width="200"/>\n            </a>\n            <div class="thumbcaption">\n             <div class="magnify">\n              <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Northrop_Grumman_Newport_News_032007_015.png" title="Enlarge">\n              </a>\n             </div>\n             Huntington Ingalls\' Newport News Shipbuilding\n            </div>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n          <p>\n           Massive\n           <a href="/wiki/Coal_pier" title="Coal pier">\n            coal piers\n           </a>\n           and loading facilities were established in the late 19th and early 20th century by the\n           <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_and_Ohio_Railway" title="Chesapeake and Ohio Railway">\n            Chesapeake and Ohio Railway\n           </a>\n           (C&amp;O),\n           <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_and_Western_Railway" title="Norfolk and Western Railway">\n            Norfolk and Western Railway\n           </a>\n           (N&amp;W), and\n           <a href="/wiki/Virginian_Railway" title="Virginian Railway">\n            Virginian Railway\n           </a>\n           (VGN). The latter two were predecessors of the\n           <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern_Railway" title="Norfolk Southern Railway">\n            Norfolk Southern Railway\n           </a>\n           , a\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_I_railroad" title="Class I railroad">\n            Class I railroad\n           </a>\n           which has its headquarters in Norfolk, and continues to export coal from a large facility at\n           <a href="/wiki/Lambert%27s_Point" title="Lambert\'s Point">\n            Lambert\'s Point\n           </a>\n           on the Elizabeth River.\n           <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">\n            CSX Transportation\n           </a>\n           now serves the former C&amp;O facility at Newport News. (The VGN\'s former coal facility at\n           <a href="/wiki/Sewell%27s_Point" title="Sewell\'s Point">\n            Sewell\'s Point\n           </a>\n           has been gone since the 1960s, and the property is now part of the expansive\n           <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Norfolk" title="Naval Station Norfolk">\n            Norfolk Navy Base\n           </a>\n           ).\n          </p>\n          <h3>\n           <span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_impact">\n            Federal impact\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Federal impact">\n             edit\n            </a>\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h3>\n          <p>\n           Almost 80% of the region\'s economy is derived from federal sources. This includes the large military presence, but also NASA and facilities of the Departments of Energy, Transportation, Commerce and Veterans Affairs. The region also receives a substantial impact in government student loans and grants, university research grants, and federal aid to cities.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The Hampton Roads area has the largest concentration of military bases and facilities of any metropolitan area in the world. Nearly one-fourth of the nation\'s active-duty military personnel are stationed in Hampton Roads, and 45% of the region\'s $81B gross regional output is Defense-related.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n            <a href="#cite_note-66">\n             [66]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n            <a href="#cite_note-67">\n             [67]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n           All five military services\' operating forces are there, as well as several major command headquarters: Hampton Roads is a chief rendezvous of the\n           <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">\n            United States Navy\n           </a>\n           , and the area is home to the\n           <a href="/wiki/Allied_Command_Transformation" title="Allied Command Transformation">\n            Allied Command Transformation\n           </a>\n           , which is the only major military command of the\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organization" title="North Atlantic Treaty Organization">\n            North Atlantic Treaty Organization\n           </a>\n           (\n           <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">\n            NATO\n           </a>\n           ) on U.S. soil.\n           <a href="/wiki/Langley_Air_Force_Base" title="Langley Air Force Base">\n            Langley Air Force Base\n           </a>\n           is home to\n           <a href="/wiki/Air_Combat_Command" title="Air Combat Command">\n            Air Combat Command\n           </a>\n           (ACC). The\n           <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Norfolk" title="Naval Station Norfolk">\n            Norfolk Navy Base\n           </a>\n           is located at\n           <a href="/wiki/Sewell%27s_Point" title="Sewell\'s Point">\n            Sewell\'s Point\n           </a>\n           near the mouth, on the site used for the tercentennial\n           <a href="/wiki/Jamestown_Exposition" title="Jamestown Exposition">\n            Jamestown Exposition\n           </a>\n           in 1907. For a width of 500 feet (150\xc2\xa0m) the Federal government during 1902 through 1905 increased its minimum depth at low water from 25.5 to 30 feet (8 to 9\xc2\xa0m), and the channel has now been dredged to a depth of 55 feet (17\xc2\xa0m) in some places.\n          </p>\n          <div class="thumb tright">\n           <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n            <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Langley_research_center.jpg">\n             <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="225" data-file-width="300" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Langley_research_center.jpg/200px-Langley_research_center.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/ff/Langley_research_center.jpg 1.5x" width="200"/>\n            </a>\n            <div class="thumbcaption">\n             <div class="magnify">\n              <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Langley_research_center.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n              </a>\n             </div>\n             NASA Langley Research Center\n            </div>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n          <p>\n           <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n            NASA\n           </a>\n           \'s\n           <a href="/wiki/Langley_Research_Center" title="Langley Research Center">\n            Langley Research Center\n           </a>\n           , located on the Peninsula adjacent to\n           <a href="/wiki/Langley_Air_Force_Base" title="Langley Air Force Base">\n            Langley Air Force Base\n           </a>\n           in Hampton, is home to scientific and aerospace technology research. The\n           <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson_National_Accelerator_Facility" title="Thomas Jefferson National Accelerator Facility">\n            Thomas Jefferson National Accelerator Facility\n           </a>\n           (commonly known as Jefferson Labs) is located nearby in Newport News.\n          </p>\n          <h3>\n           <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_growth">\n            Commercial growth\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Commercial growth">\n             edit\n            </a>\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h3>\n          <p>\n           The area\'s experiences with commercial and retail centers began early in 1918. Afton Square, located in the\n           <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">\n            Cradock\n           </a>\n           naval community of Portsmouth, was the first planned shopping center in the USA and has served as template for future developments throughout the nation.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n            <a href="#cite_note-68">\n             [68]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           Hampton Roads experienced tremendous growth during and after World War II. In the 1950s, a trend in retail was the shopping center, a group of stores along a common sidewalk adjacent to off-street parking, usually in a suburban location.\n          </p>\n          <div class="thumb tright">\n           <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n            <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LynnhavenOutdoor.JPG">\n             <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="200" data-file-width="300" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e4/LynnhavenOutdoor.JPG/200px-LynnhavenOutdoor.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/e4/LynnhavenOutdoor.JPG 1.5x" width="200"/>\n            </a>\n            <div class="thumbcaption">\n             <div class="magnify">\n              <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LynnhavenOutdoor.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n              </a>\n             </div>\n             Lynnhaven Mall, opened in 1981, has 1,400,000 square feet (130,000\xc2\xa0m\n             <sup>\n              2\n             </sup>\n             ) and 180 stores.\n            </div>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n          <p>\n           In 1959, one of the largest on the east coast of the USA was opened at the northeast corner of Military Highway and Virginia Beach Boulevard on property which had formally been used as an airfield. The new\n           <a href="/wiki/JANAF_Shopping_Center" title="JANAF Shopping Center">\n            JANAF Shopping Center\n           </a>\n           , located in Norfolk, featured acres of free parking and dozens of stores. Backed by retired military personnel, the name JANAF was an acronym for Joint Army Navy Air Force.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n            <a href="#cite_note-69">\n             [69]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           During the 1950s and early 1960s, other shopping centers in Hampton Roads were developed, such as Wards Corner Shopping Center, Downtown Plaza Shopping Center and Southern Shopping Center in Norfolk; Mid-City Shopping Center in Portsmouth; Hilltop Shopping Center (now known as\n           <a href="/wiki/The_Shops_at_Hilltop" title="The Shops at Hilltop">\n            The Shops at Hilltop\n           </a>\n           ) in Virginia Beach; Riverdale Shopping Center in Hampton and the Warwick-Denbigh Shopping Center in Newport News.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           In the late-1960s, a new type of shopping center came to Hampton Roads: the Indoor Shopping Mall. In 1965, South Hampton Roads broke ground on its first shopping mall in Virginia Beach, known as\n           <a href="/wiki/Pembroke_Mall" title="Pembroke Mall">\n            Pembroke Mall\n           </a>\n           . The mall opened in 1966, and became Hampton Road\'s newest indoor shopping destination. The\n           <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Peninsula" title="Virginia Peninsula">\n            Virginia Peninsula\n           </a>\n           had its first indoor shopping mall in 1973, with\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coliseum_Mall" title="Coliseum Mall">\n            Coliseum Mall\n           </a>\n           . Coliseum Mall drew so much traffic from\n           <a href="/wiki/Interstate_64" title="Interstate 64">\n            Interstate 64\n           </a>\n           , that a towering\n           <a href="/wiki/Overpass" title="Overpass">\n            flyover\n           </a>\n           was built at the Mercury Boulevard and Coliseum Drive intersection, to accommodate eastbound mall traffic, from the Mercury Boulevard interchange. Coliseum Mall was demolished to make way for the open air mixed-use development\n           <a href="/wiki/Peninsula_Town_Center" title="Peninsula Town Center">\n            Peninsula Town Center\n           </a>\n           . Also in the 1970s,\n           <a href="/wiki/Tower_Mall" title="Tower Mall">\n            Tower Mall\n           </a>\n           was built in Portsmouth, but was torn down and turned into the Victory Crossing shopping development. In Norfolk,\n           <a href="/wiki/Military_Circle_Mall" title="Military Circle Mall">\n            Military Circle Mall\n           </a>\n           on\n           <a href="/wiki/Military_Highway" title="Military Highway">\n            Military Highway\n           </a>\n           was built across\n           <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach_Boulevard" title="Virginia Beach Boulevard">\n            Virginia Beach Boulevard\n           </a>\n           from the large JANAF Shopping Center with its own high-rise hotel right in the center. In 1981,\n           <a href="/wiki/Greenbrier_Mall" title="Greenbrier Mall">\n            Greenbrier Mall\n           </a>\n           gave Chesapeake a shopping mall of its own as well, and Virginia Beach got the massive Lynnhaven Mall the same year.\n          </p>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Square_Mall" title="Chesapeake Square Mall">\n           Chesapeake Square Mall\n          </a>\n          was constructed in Chesapeake, Virginia in 1989, near the border of Suffolk, Virginia, and has spawned a number of shopping centers in the surrounding areas.\n          <div class="thumb tright">\n           <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n            <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macarthercenter.JPG">\n             <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Macarthercenter.JPG/200px-Macarthercenter.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Macarthercenter.JPG/300px-Macarthercenter.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Macarthercenter.JPG/400px-Macarthercenter.JPG 2x" width="200"/>\n            </a>\n            <div class="thumbcaption">\n             <div class="magnify">\n              <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macarthercenter.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n              </a>\n             </div>\n             MacArthur Center, opened in 1999, has 1,100,000 square feet (100,000\xc2\xa0m\n             <sup>\n              2\n             </sup>\n             ) and 140 stores.\n            </div>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n          <p>\n           <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Center" title="MacArthur Center">\n            MacArthur Center\n           </a>\n           opened in March 1999, which made downtown Norfolk a prime shoppers destination, with the region\'s first\n           <a href="/wiki/Nordstrom" title="Nordstrom">\n            Nordstrom\n           </a>\n           department store anchor. MacArthur Center is compared to other downtown malls, such as Baltimore\'s\n           <a href="/wiki/Harborplace" title="Harborplace">\n            Harborplace\n           </a>\n           , Indianapolis\'\n           <a href="/wiki/Circle_Centre" title="Circle Centre">\n            Circle Centre\n           </a>\n           Mall, Atlanta\'s\n           <a href="/wiki/Lenox_Square" title="Lenox Square">\n            Lenox Square\n           </a>\n           Mall and most comparably to\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fashion_Centre_at_Pentagon_City" title="Fashion Centre at Pentagon City">\n            The Fashion Centre at Pentagon City\n           </a>\n           near Washington, D.C., in\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arlington,_Virginia" title="Arlington, Virginia">\n            Arlington, Virginia\n           </a>\n           .\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           Currently, Virginia Beach\'s\n           <a href="/wiki/Lynnhaven_Mall" title="Lynnhaven Mall">\n            Lynnhaven Mall\n           </a>\n           is the region\'s largest shopping center with nearly 180 stores, and is one of the region\'s biggest tourist draws, with the\n           <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach_Oceanfront" title="Virginia Beach Oceanfront">\n            Virginia Beach Oceanfront\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Williamsburg" title="Colonial Williamsburg">\n            Colonial Williamsburg\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Busch_Gardens_Williamsburg" title="Busch Gardens Williamsburg">\n            Busch Gardens Williamsburg\n           </a>\n           and MacArthur Center.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           For a long time, the indoor shopping malls were seen as largely competitive with small shopping centers and traditional downtown type areas. However, in the 1990s and since, the "\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big-box" title="Big-box">\n            big-box\n           </a>\n           stores" on the Peninsula and Southside, such as Wal-mart, Home Depot, and Target have been creating a new competitive atmosphere for the shopping malls of Hampton Roads.\n          </p>\n          <div class="thumb tright">\n           <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n            <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Henry_Mall_sign,_Hampton_Roads,_Virginia.jpg">\n             <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Patrick_Henry_Mall_sign%2C_Hampton_Roads%2C_Virginia.jpg/200px-Patrick_Henry_Mall_sign%2C_Hampton_Roads%2C_Virginia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Patrick_Henry_Mall_sign%2C_Hampton_Roads%2C_Virginia.jpg/300px-Patrick_Henry_Mall_sign%2C_Hampton_Roads%2C_Virginia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Patrick_Henry_Mall_sign%2C_Hampton_Roads%2C_Virginia.jpg/400px-Patrick_Henry_Mall_sign%2C_Hampton_Roads%2C_Virginia.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n            </a>\n            <div class="thumbcaption">\n             <div class="magnify">\n              <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Henry_Mall_sign,_Hampton_Roads,_Virginia.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n              </a>\n             </div>\n             Patrick Henry Mall, opened in 1987, has 714,310 square feet (66,362\xc2\xa0m\n             <sup>\n              2\n             </sup>\n             ) and 120+ stores\n            </div>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n          <p>\n           Several older malls such as Pembroke and Military Circle have since their grand openings been renovated, and others have been closed and torn down. Newmarket North Mall is now\n           <a href="/wiki/NetCenter" title="NetCenter">\n            NetCenter\n           </a>\n           , a business center (the Sears store remains).\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coliseum_Mall" title="Coliseum Mall">\n            Coliseum Mall\n           </a>\n           , in Hampton, has been redeveloped as\n           <a href="/wiki/Peninsula_Town_Center" title="Peninsula Town Center">\n            Peninsula Town Center\n           </a>\n           in a new style, in step with the latest commercial real estate trend: the nationwide establishment of "\n           <a href="/wiki/Lifestyle_center_(retail)" title="Lifestyle center (retail)">\n            lifestyle centers\n           </a>\n           ". Additional malls which have closed include\n           <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Plaza_Mall" title="Mercury Plaza Mall">\n            Mercury Mall\n           </a>\n           in Hampton (converted to Mercury Plaza Shopping Center in the mid-1980s, then completely torn down in 2001), and\n           <a href="/wiki/Tower_Mall" title="Tower Mall">\n            Tower Mall\n           </a>\n           in Portsmouth (Built in the early 1970s, then torn down in 2001).\n          </p>\n          <table class="wikitable" style="width:550px;">\n           <tr>\n            <th>\n             Shopping         </td>\n           </tr>\n           <tr>\n            <td>\n             <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Gallery_at_Military_Circle" title="The Gallery at Military Circle">\n              The Gallery at Military Circle\n             </a>\n            </td>\n            <td>\n             <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">\n              Norfolk\n
