         <sup>\n              2\n             </sup>\n             )\n            </td>\n            <td>\n             1966\n            </td>\n           </tr>\n          </table>\n          <h3>\n           <span id="America\'s_first_region">\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-headline" id="America.27s_first_region">\n            America\'s first region\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: America\'s first region">\n             edit\n            </a>\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h3>\n          <p>\n           In late 2006, the Hampton Roads Partnership, a non-profit organization representing 17 localities (ten cities, six counties, and one town), all local universities and major military commands as well as leading businesses in southeastern Virginia, commenced a campaign aimed at branding the land area of Hampton Roads as "America\'s First Region".\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The new title is based on events in 1607 when English\n           <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Newport" title="Christopher Newport">\n            Captain Christopher Newport\'s\n           </a>\n           three ships \xe2\x80\x93 the\n           <i>\n            <a href="/wiki/Susan_Constant" title="Susan Constant">\n             Susan Constant\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           ,\n           <i>\n            <a href="/wiki/Godspeed_(ship)" title="Godspeed (ship)">\n             Godspeed\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           , and\n           <i>\n            <a href="/wiki/Discovery_(1602_ship)" title="Discovery (1602 ship)">\n             Discovery\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           landed at\n           <a href="/wiki/Cape_Henry" title="Cape Henry">\n            Cape Henry\n           </a>\n           along the Atlantic Coast in what is today Virginia Beach. After 18 days of exploring the area, the ships and their crews arrived at\n           <a href="/wiki/Jamestown_Island" title="Jamestown Island">\n            Jamestown Island\n           </a>\n           where they established the first English speaking settlement to survive in the\n           <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">\n            New World\n           </a>\n           on May 14, 1607.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           Because the region\'s east-west boundaries (now the City of Virginia Beach and James City County) have not changed since 1607, the Partnership felt justified in labeling Hampton Roads "America\'s First Region". It unveiled the new brand before 800 people at the annual meeting of the Hampton Roads Chamber of Commerce on December 13, 2006. A video shown that afternoon included endorsements from mayors and county board of supervisors chairs representing Hampton, Norfolk, Virginia Beach, Williamsburg and James City County as well as the\n           <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Virginia" title="Governor of Virginia">\n            Governor of Virginia\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timothy_Kaine" title="Timothy Kaine">\n            Timothy Kaine\n           </a>\n           .\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n            <a href="#cite_note-70">\n             [70]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n           <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n            [\n            <i>\n             <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n              <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2008)">\n               citation needed\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </i>\n            ]\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The mission of Hampton Roads Economic Development Alliance (HREDA) is a non-profit organization dedicated to business attraction\xe2\x80\x94marketing the Hampton Roads region as the preferred location for business investment and expansion. HREDA represents the cities of Chesapeake, Hampton, Newport News, Norfolk, Poquoson, Portsmouth, Suffolk, Virginia Beach, Williamsburg and Franklin, as well as the counties of Gloucester, James City, Isle of Wight, York, and Southampton.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HREDA_71-0">\n            <a href="#cite_note-HREDA-71">\n             [71]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <h2>\n           <span class="mw-headline" id="Flag">\n            Flag\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Flag">\n             edit\n            </a>\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h2>\n          <div class="thumb tright">\n           <div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;">\n            <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Hampton_Roads,_Virginia.svg">\n             <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Flag_of_Hampton_Roads%2C_Virginia.svg/275px-Flag_of_Hampton_Roads%2C_Virginia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Flag_of_Hampton_Roads%2C_Virginia.svg/413px-Flag_of_Hampton_Roads%2C_Virginia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Flag_of_Hampton_Roads%2C_Virginia.svg/550px-Flag_of_Hampton_Roads%2C_Virginia.svg.png 2x" width="275"/>\n            </a>\n            <div class="thumbcaption">\n             <div class="magnify">\n              <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Hampton_Roads,_Virginia.svg" title="Enlarge">\n              </a>\n             </div>\n             Hampton Roads flag, adopted 1998\n            </div>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n          <p>\n           In 1998, a flag representing the Hampton Roads region was adopted. The design of the flag was created by a contest. The winner, sixteen-year-old Andrew J. Wall of\n           <a href="/wiki/Frank_W._Cox_High_School" title="Frank W. Cox High School">\n            Frank W. Cox High School\n           </a>\n           in Virginia Beach, raised the new regional flag for the first time on the mast of a ship moored in the harbor.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           As conceived by student Andrew Wall and embellished by the selection committee, his flag is highly symbolic:\n          </p>\n          <dl>\n           <dd>\n            The ring of sixteen white stars stands for the cities and counties that comprise the region of Hampton Roads. The blue upper panel refers to the sea and sky, recalling the first European settlers at Jamestown in 1607, the first battle between ironclad ships in 1862, the importance of shipbuilding and ship repair in the area, as well as maritime commerce, fishing, recreational boating, and the major military and government installations around the area\'s shores. Agriculture, the environment, tourism, industry, and a healthy quality of life are suggested by the lower panel of green. The wavy white central band with three crests suggests past, present, and future. The wave also recalls the surf and sand dunes of the area as seen from the sea. Water is the central theme. It touches all the components and binds them together.\n            <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n             <a href="#cite_note-72">\n              [72]\n             </a>\n            </sup>\n           </dd>\n          </dl>\n          <h2>\n           <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">\n            Culture\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Culture">\n             edit\n            </a>\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h2>\n          <div class="thumb tright">\n           <div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;">\n            <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Triangle_Virginia_PNG.png">\n             <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="948" data-file-width="1431" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Historic_Triangle_Virginia_PNG.png/275px-Historic_Triangle_Virginia_PNG.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Historic_Triangle_Virginia_PNG.png/413px-Historic_Triangle_Virginia_PNG.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Historic_Triangle_Virginia_PNG.png/550px-Historic_Triangle_Virginia_PNG.png 2x" width="275"/>\n            </a>\n            <div class="thumbcaption">\n             <div class="magnify">\n              <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Triangle_Virginia_PNG.png" title="Enlarge">\n              </a>\n             </div>\n             Virginia\'s Historic Triangle\n            </div>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n          <p>\n           The area is most often associated with the larger\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_South" title="American South">\n            American South\n           </a>\n           . People who have grown up in the Hampton Roads area have a unique\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidewater_accent" title="Tidewater accent">\n            Tidewater accent\n           </a>\n           which sounds different from a stereotypical\n           <a href="/wiki/Southern_American_English" title="Southern American English">\n            Southern accent\n           </a>\n           . Vowels have a longer pronunciation than in a regular southern accent.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Virginia_Accents_73-0">\n            <a href="#cite_note-Virginia_Accents-73">\n             [73]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <h3>\n           <span id="Attractions,_museums_and_sites_of_interest">\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-headline" id="Attractions.2C_museums_and_sites_of_interest">\n            Attractions, museums and sites of interest\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Attractions, museums and sites of interest">\n             edit\n            </a>\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h3>\n          <p>\n           There\'s also a wealth of other points of history to explore in the Hampton Roads area. Led by the Historic Triangle area, Hampton Roads consistently rates among the top tourism destinations in the world.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           Cultural attractions include museums, historical sites, and venues from tiny to massively large for such things as art and musical shows. The region hosts two week-long visits by the\n           <a href="/wiki/Ringling_Bros._and_Barnum_%26_Bailey_Circus" title="Ringling Bros. and Barnum &amp; Bailey Circus">\n            Ringling Bros. and Barnum &amp; Bailey Circus\n           </a>\n           each year with multiple performances at Norfolk Scope and the Hampton Coliseum, and even attracts a group of\n           <a class="external text" href="http://finance.groups.yahoo.com/group/CircusTrain/" rel="nofollow">\n            Circus Train Enthusiasts\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Railfan" title="Railfan">\n            railfans\n           </a>\n           who watch, photograph and report on the blue or red unit trains as they make their move between the two sites, requiring a long inland trip through\n           <a href="/wiki/Petersburg,_Virginia" title="Petersburg, Virginia">\n            Petersburg\n           </a>\n           and\n           <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">\n            Richmond\n           </a>\n           in order to avoid crossing the 10-mile (16\xc2\xa0km) geographical distance across the harbor (a trip impassable directly by modern trains; the two\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bridge-tunnel" title="Bridge-tunnel">\n            bridge-tunnel\n           </a>\n           facilities operated by\n           <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Department_of_Transportation" title="Virginia Department of Transportation">\n            VDOT\n           </a>\n           accommodate only highway traffic).\n          </p>\n          <h4>\n           <span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_Triangle">\n            Historic Triangle\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Historic Triangle">\n             edit\n            </a>\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h4>\n          <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation">\n           <tr>\n            <td class="mbox-image">\n             <div style="width:52px">\n              <img alt="" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>\n             </div>\n            </td>\n            <td class="mbox-text">\n             <div class="mbox-text-span">\n              This article\n              <b>\n               is written like a\n               <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTTRAVEL" title="Wikipedia:NOTTRAVEL">\n                travel guide\n               </a>\n               rather than an encyclopedic description of the subject\n              </b>\n              .\n              <span class="hide-when-compact">\n               Please\n               <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit">\n                help improve it\n               </a>\n               by rewriting it in an\n               <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Encyclopedic_style" title="Wikipedia:Encyclopedic style">\n                encyclopedic style\n               </a>\n               . If a travel guide is intended, use of\n               <a href="/wiki/Wikivoyage" title="Wikivoyage">\n                Wikivoyage\n               </a>\n               is strongly suggested.\n              </span>\n              <small>\n               <i>\n                (April 2013)\n               </i>\n              </small>\n             </div>\n            </td>\n           </tr>\n          </table>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a href="/wiki/Historic_Triangle" title="Historic Triangle">\n            Historic Triangle\n           </a>\n           is located on the\n           <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Peninsula" title="Virginia Peninsula">\n            Virginia Peninsula\n           </a>\n           and includes the colonial communities of\n           <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">\n            Jamestown\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n            Williamsburg\n           </a>\n           , and\n           <a href="/wiki/Yorktown,_Virginia" title="Yorktown, Virginia">\n            Yorktown\n           </a>\n           , with many restored attractions linked by the\n           <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Parkway" title="Colonial Parkway">\n            Colonial Parkway\n           </a>\n           .\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">\n            National Park Service\n           </a>\n           \'s\n           <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Parkway" title="Colonial Parkway">\n            Colonial Parkway\n           </a>\n           joins the three popular attractions of Colonial Virginia with a scenic and bucolic roadway carefully shielded from views of commercial development. This helps visitors mentally return to the past, and there are often views of\n           <a href="/wiki/Wildlife" title="Wildlife">\n            wildlife\n           </a>\n           and\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waterfowl" title="Waterfowl">\n            waterfowl\n           </a>\n           . This two lane roadway is the best (but not quickest) way to move between the three points. Near the James River and\n           <a href="/wiki/York_River_(Virginia)" title="York River (Virginia)">\n            York River\n           </a>\n           ends of the parkway, there are several pull-offs, where some families allow their children to feed bread to the seagulls. Commercial vehicles, except for tour buses, are prohibited.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           For an even better experience, approach the area from the south by water from\n           <a href="/wiki/Surry_County,_Virginia" title="Surry County, Virginia">\n            Surry County\n           </a>\n           with a ride aboard one of the\n           <a href="/wiki/Jamestown_Ferry" title="Jamestown Ferry">\n            Jamestown Ferrys\n           </a>\n           , which include the\n           <i>\n            Pocahontas\n           </i>\n           and\n           <i>\n            Williamsburg\n           </i>\n           . As passengers cross, they can walk about the boat or go up to an enclosed viewing level with restrooms. Weather and daylight permitting, passengers usually see\n           <a href="/wiki/Jamestown_Island" title="Jamestown Island">\n            Jamestown Island\n           </a>\n           much as the first colonists may have approached it. In fact, the replicas of\n           <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Newport" title="Christopher Newport">\n            Christopher Newport\n           </a>\n           \'s the three tiny ships,\n           <i>\n            Susan Constant\n           </i>\n           ,\n           <i>\n            Godspeed\n           </i>\n           , and\n           <i>\n            Discovery\n           </i>\n           are docked near the northern ferry landing at\n           <a href="/wiki/Glass_House_Point" title="Glass House Point">\n            Glass House Point\n           </a>\n           . Both the Jamestown Ferry and Colonial Parkway are toll-free.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The first permanent English settlement in the New World which was established at\n           <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">\n            Jamestown\n           </a>\n           in 1607. The 350th anniversary celebration at\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamestown_Festival_Park" title="Jamestown Festival Park">\n            Jamestown Festival Park\n           </a>\n           in 1957 was so popular, tourism has been continuously increasing ever since. The 400th anniversary was celebrated with an 18-month-long celebration called\n           <a href="/wiki/Jamestown_2007" title="Jamestown 2007">\n            Jamestown 2007\n           </a>\n           .\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           Today, at Jamestown, you can visit recreations of an\n           <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">\n            American Indian\n           </a>\n           village and colonial fort, and archaeological sites where current work is underway by\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaeologist" title="Archaeologist">\n            archaeologists\n           </a>\n           from the\n           <a href="/wiki/Jamestown_Rediscovery" title="Jamestown Rediscovery">\n            Jamestown Rediscovery\n           </a>\n           project, with recently recovered archaeological artifacts in a new display building. Replicas of the three ships,\n           <i>\n            <a href="/wiki/Susan_Constant" title="Susan Constant">\n             Susan Constant\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           ,\n           <i>\n            <a href="/wiki/Godspeed_(ship)" title="Godspeed (ship)">\n             Godspeed\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           , and\n           <i>\n            <a href="/wiki/Discovery_(1602_ship)" title="Discovery (1602 ship)">\n             Discovery\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           are docked nearby.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The two major attractions, which are complementary to each other, are the state-sponsored\n           <a href="/wiki/Jamestown_Settlement" title="Jamestown Settlement">\n            Jamestown Settlement\n           </a>\n           near the entrance to Jamestown Island, and the National Park Service\'s\n           <a href="/wiki/Historic_Jamestowne" title="Historic Jamestowne">\n            Historic Jamestowne\n           </a>\n           , on Jamestown Island itself.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           In 1699, the first capital of Virginia was moved to\n           <a href="/wiki/Middle_Plantation_(Virginia)" title="Middle Plantation (Virginia)">\n            Middle Plantation\n           </a>\n           at the suggestion of students from the\n           <a href="/wiki/College_of_William_%26_Mary" title="College of William &amp; Mary">\n            College of William &amp; Mary\n           </a>\n           (established 1693). It was soon renamed to\n           <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n            Williamsburg\n           </a>\n           , but became a largely forgotten little town after the capital was moved to\n           <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">\n            Richmond\n           </a>\n           in 1780. Largely due to the 20th-century preservation efforts of\n           <a href="/wiki/W._A._R._Goodwin" title="W. A. R. Goodwin">\n            W. A. R. Goodwin\n           </a>\n           , rector of\n           <a href="/wiki/Bruton_Parish_Church" title="Bruton Parish Church">\n            Bruton Parish Church\n           </a>\n           and the generosity of\n           <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">\n            Standard Oil\n           </a>\n           heir\n           <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller_Jr." title="John D. Rockefeller Jr.">\n            John D. Rockefeller Jr.\n           </a>\n           , today\n           <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Williamsburg" title="Colonial Williamsburg">\n            Colonial Williamsburg\n           </a>\n           is a large\n           <a href="/wiki/Living_museum" title="Living museum">\n            living museum\n           </a>\n           of early American life. It has dozens of restored and recreated buildings and reenactors. It is one of the most popular tourist destinations in the world. The Visitor\'s Center (right off the Colonial Parkway) features a short movie and is an excellent place to start (and leave automobiles, which are restricted from the restored area, where wheelchair-accessible shuttle\n           <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">\n            bus\n           </a>\n           service is provided).\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           <a href="/wiki/Bassett_Hall" title="Bassett Hall">\n            Bassett Hall\n           </a>\n           , an 18th-century farmhouse, is located in Williamsburg just southeast of the Historic Area, was the Williamsburg home for over 25 years of the family of John D. Rockefeller Jr and his family from the mid-1930s until 1960, following over 7 years of restoration and expansions. The Rockefeller family bequeathed Bassett Hall to Colonial Williamsburg in 1979.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n            <a href="#cite_note-74">\n             [74]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n           The home is now open to the public and appears much as it did in the 1930s and 1940s when the Rockefellers made it their home.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n            <a href="#cite_note-75">\n             [75]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The third point of the Historic Triangle of Colonial Virginia is\n           <a href="/wiki/Yorktown,_Virginia" title="Yorktown, Virginia">\n            Yorktown\n           </a>\n           where General Cornwallis surrendered to\n           <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">\n            George Washington\n           </a>\n           in 1781, ending the\n           <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">\n            American Revolution\n           </a>\n           . There are two large visitor centers, battlefield drives, and a waterfront area.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           Notwithstanding the amazingly successful efforts to provide a non-commercial atmosphere at the three Historic Triangle areas (and on the Colonial Parkway between them), there are many hotels, motels, campgrounds, restaurants, shops and stores, gasoline stations, and amusements close by.\n          </p>\n          <ul>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Busch_Gardens_Williamsburg" title="Busch Gardens Williamsburg">\n             Busch Gardens Williamsburg\n            </a>\n            is a major theme park located near\n            <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n             Williamsburg\n            </a>\n            in\n            <a href="/wiki/James_City_County,_Virginia" title="James City County, Virginia">\n             James City County\n            </a>\n            .\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            Williamsburg Pottery Factory is also nearby on\n            <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_60_in_Virginia" title="U.S. Route 60 in Virginia">\n             U.S. Route 60\n            </a>\n            , seven miles (11\xc2\xa0km) west of\n            <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n             Williamsburg\n            </a>\n            in\n            <a href="/wiki/James_City_County,_Virginia" title="James City County, Virginia">\n             James City County\n            </a>\n            .\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n          <h4>\n           <span class="mw-headline" id="Peninsula_museums">\n            Peninsula museums\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Peninsula museums">\n             edit\n            </a>\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h4>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a href="/wiki/Mariners%27_Museum" title="Mariners\' Museum">\n            Mariners\' Museum\n           </a>\n           , founded in 1930 by\n           <a href="/wiki/Archer_Milton_Huntington" title="Archer Milton Huntington">\n            Archer\n           </a>\n           and\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anna_Huntington" title="Anna Huntington">\n            Anna Huntington\n           </a>\n           , is an institution dedicated to bringing maritime history to the world. It is currently home to the\n           <a href="/wiki/USS_Monitor" title="USS Monitor">\n            USS\n            <i>\n             Monitor\n            </i>\n           </a>\n           Center where 210 tons of artifacts recovered from the USS\n           <i>\n            Monitor\n           </i>\n           are held, including the\n           <a href="/wiki/Gun_turret" title="Gun turret">\n            gun turret\n           </a>\n           . The museum also consists of a 550-acre park and\n           <a href="/wiki/Lake_Maury" title="Lake Maury">\n            Lake Maury\n           </a>\n           , through which is the five-mile Noland Trail. The permanent collection at the museum totals about 32,000 objects, equally divided between works of art and three-dimensional objects. The Mariners\' Museum Library and Archive, now located in the Trible Library at\n           <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Newport_University" title="Christopher Newport University">\n            Christopher Newport University\n           </a>\n           , consists of over 78,000 books, 800,000 photographs, films and negatives, and over one million archival pieces, making it the largest maritime library in the Western Hemisphere.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n            <a href="#cite_note-76">\n             [76]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a href="/wiki/Virginia_War_Museum" title="Virginia War Museum">\n            Virginia War Museum\n           </a>\n           covers American military history. The museum\'s collection includes, weapons, vehicles, artifacts, uniforms and posters from various periods of American history. Highlights of the museum\'s collection include a section of the\n           <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">\n            Berlin Wall\n           </a>\n           and the outer wall from\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dachau_Concentration_Camp" title="Dachau Concentration Camp">\n            Dachau Concentration Camp\n           </a>\n           .\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n            <a href="#cite_note-77">\n             [77]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Living_Museum" title="Virginia Living Museum">\n            Virginia Living Museum\n           </a>\n           , first established in 1966, combines the elements of a native wildlife park, science museum, aquarium, botanical preserve, and planetarium. The exhibits are themed on the geographic regions of Virginia, from the Appalachian Mountains to the offshore waters of the Atlantic Ocean, and includes more than 245 different animal species.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n            <a href="#cite_note-78">\n             [78]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a href="/wiki/Peninsula_Fine_Arts_Center" title="Peninsula Fine Arts Center">\n            Peninsula Fine Arts Center\n           </a>\n           in Newport News contains a rotating gallery of art exhibits. The center also contains a Studio Art School of private and group instruction for all ages. It maintains a permanent "Hands On For Kids" gallery designed for children and families to interact in what the center describes as "a fun, educational environment that encourages participation with art materials and concepts."\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n            <a href="#cite_note-79">\n             [79]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a href="/wiki/Hampton_University" title="Hampton University">\n            Hampton University\n           </a>\n           museum was established in 1868 in the heart of the historic Hampton University campus. The museum is the oldest African American museum in the United States and one of the oldest museums in the State of Virginia. It contains over 9,000 objects, including African American fine arts, traditional African, Native American, Native Hawaiian, Pacific Island, and Asian art.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n            <a href="#cite_note-80">\n             [80]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The Charles H. Taylor Arts Center is Hampton\'s public access arts center. It offers a series of changing visual art exhibitions as well as a quarterly schedule of classes, workshops and educational programs.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n            <a href="#cite_note-81">\n             [81]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The Downing-Gross Cultural Arts Center in SE Newport News contains a community-based art gallery, as well as arts classrooms and the Ella Fitzgerald Theater.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n            <a href="#cite_note-82">\n             [82]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The Casemate Museum (where former\n           <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">\n            Confederate\n           </a>\n           President\n           <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Davis" title="Jefferson Davis">\n            Jefferson Davis\n           </a>\n           was imprisoned) is at\n           <a href="/wiki/Fort_Monroe" title="Fort Monroe">\n            Fort Monroe\n           </a>\n           in the historic\n           <a href="/wiki/Phoebus,_Virginia" title="Phoebus, Virginia">\n            Phoebus\n           </a>\n           area at\n           <a href="/wiki/Old_Point_Comfort" title="Old Point Comfort">\n            Old Point Comfort\n           </a>\n           in\n           <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Virginia" title="Hampton, Virginia">\n            Hampton\n           </a>\n           .\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fort_Monroe_83-0">\n            <a href="#cite_note-Fort_Monroe-83">\n             [83]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n            NASA\n           </a>\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASA_Langley" title="NASA Langley">\n            Langley Research Center\n           </a>\n           is in Hampton, the original training ground for the\n           <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Seven" title="Mercury Seven">\n            Mercury Seven\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Project_Gemini" title="Project Gemini">\n            Gemini\n           </a>\n           , and\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Project_Apollo" title="Project Apollo">\n            Apollo\n           </a>\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astronauts" title="Astronauts">\n            Astronauts\n           </a>\n           . Visitors are able to learn about the region\'s aviation history at the\n           <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Air_and_Space_Center" title="Virginia Air and Space Center">\n            Virginia Air and Space Center\n           </a>\n           in\n           <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Virginia" title="Hampton, Virginia">\n            Hampton\n           </a>\n           .\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VASC_84-0">\n            <a href="#cite_note-VASC-84">\n             [84]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           Air Power Park is an outdoor on-site display of various aircraft and a space capsule. It is located on Mercury Boulevard at the intersection of LaSalle Blvd, near the AF Base.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The Biblical Art Gallery at Ivy Farms Baptist Church is Virginia\'s largest collection of pre-1900s religious art.\n          </p>\n          <h3>\n           <span class="mw-headline" id="Harbor_tour_sites">\n            Harbor tour sites\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Harbor tour sites">\n             edit\n            </a>\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h3>\n          <ul>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Fort_Wool" title="Fort Wool">\n             Fort Wool\n            </a>\n            is located in the middle of the Hampton Roads harbor. Harbor tours departing from\n            <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Virginia" title="Hampton, Virginia">\n             Hampton\n            </a>\n            and\n            <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">\n             Newport News\n            </a>\n            provide access to\n            <a href="/wiki/Fort_Wool" title="Fort Wool">\n             Fort Wool\n            </a>\n            .\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            Newport News Shipbuilding \xe2\x80\x93 America\'s largest military shipbuilder \xe2\x80\x93 may also been seem from aboard a Hampton-based harbor tour.\n            <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miss_Hampton_II_85-0">\n             <a href="#cite_note-Miss_Hampton_II-85">\n              [85]\n             </a>\n            </sup>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n          <h4>\n           <span class="mw-headline" id="South_Hampton_Roads">\n            South Hampton Roads\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: South Hampton Roads">\n             edit\n            </a>\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h4>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a href="/wiki/Chrysler_Museum_of_Art" title="Chrysler Museum of Art">\n            Chrysler Museum of Art\n           </a>\n           , located in the\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghent_district" title="Ghent district">\n            Ghent district\n           </a>\n           of Norfolk, is the region\'s foremost art museum and is considered by\n           <i>\n            <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">\n             The New York Times\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           to be the finest in the state.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norfolk_Travel_Guide_86-0">\n            <a href="#cite_note-Norfolk_Travel_Guide-86">\n             [86]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n           Of particular note is the extensive glass collection and American\n           <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">\n            neoclassical\n           </a>\n           marble sculptures.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           <a href="/wiki/Nauticus" title="Nauticus">\n            Nauticus\n           </a>\n           , the National Maritime Center, opened on the downtown waterfront in 1994. It features hands-on exhibits, interactive theaters,\n           <a href="/wiki/Aquarium" title="Aquarium">\n            aquaria\n           </a>\n           , digital high-definition films and an extensive variety of educational programs. Since 2000, Nauticus has been home to the battleship\n           <a href="/wiki/USS_Wisconsin_(BB-64)" title="USS Wisconsin (BB-64)">\n            USS\n            <i>\n             Wisconsin\n            </i>\n           </a>\n           , one of the last battleships to be built in the United States. It served briefly in World War II and later in the\n           <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">\n            Korean\n           </a>\n           and\n           <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">\n            Gulf Wars\n           </a>\n           .\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nauticus_87-0">\n            <a href="#cite_note-Nauticus-87">\n             [87]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n           The General\n           <a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">\n            Douglas MacArthur\n           </a>\n           Memorial, located in the 19th-century Norfolk court house and city hall in downtown, contains the tombs of the late General and his wife, a museum and a vast research library, personal belongings (including his famous corncob pipe) and a short film that chronicles the life of the famous\n           <a href="/wiki/General_of_the_Army_(United_States)" title="General of the Army (United States)">\n            General of the Army\n           </a>\n           .\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MacArthur_Memorial_88-0">\n            <a href="#cite_note-MacArthur_Memorial-88">\n             [88]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           Also in downtown Norfolk and inside Nauticus is the\n           <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads_Naval_Museum" title="Hampton Roads Naval Museum">\n            Hampton Roads Naval Museum\n           </a>\n           , an official U.S. Navy museum that focuses on the 220 plus year history of the Navy within the region.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Museum_of_Virginia" title="Children\'s Museum of Virginia">\n            Children\'s Museum of Virginia\n           </a>\n           in\n           <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">\n            Portsmouth\n           </a>\n           has one of the largest collection of model electric trains and other toys.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Naval_Shipyard" title="Norfolk Naval Shipyard">\n            Norfolk Naval Shipyard\n           </a>\n           in\n           <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">\n            Portsmouth\n           </a>\n           is one of the oldest shipyards and has the first\n           <a href="/wiki/Dry_dock" title="Dry dock">\n            dry dock\n           </a>\n           on display.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a href="/wiki/Great_Dismal_Swamp_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Great Dismal Swamp National Wildlife Refuge">\n            Great Dismal Swamp National Wildlife Refuge\n           </a>\n           (in Suffolk and Chesapeake) is accessed from\n           <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_17" title="U.S. Route 17">\n            U.S. Route 17\n           </a>\n           in\n           <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake,_Virginia" title="Chesapeake, Virginia">\n            Chesapeake\n           </a>\n           .\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Suffolk-Nansemond_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Suffolk-Nansemond Museum (page does not exist)">\n            Suffolk-Nansemond Museum\n           </a>\n           is in the restored\n           <a href="/wiki/Seaboard_Air_Line_Railroad" title="Seaboard Air Line Railroad">\n            Seaboard\n           </a>\n           and\n           <a href="/wiki/Virginian_Railway" title="Virginian Railway">\n            Virginian Railway\n           </a>\n           passenger train station in\n           <a href="/wiki/Suffolk,_Virginia" title="Suffolk, Virginia">\n            Suffolk\n           </a>\n           .\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Wight_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Isle of Wight Museum (page does not exist)">\n            Isle of Wight Museum\n           </a>\n           is in\n           <a href="/wiki/Smithfield,_Virginia" title="Smithfield, Virginia">\n            Smithfield\n           </a>\n           .\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The Contemporary Art Center of Virginia located in Virginia Beach features the significant art of our time.\n          </p>\n          <h3>\n           <span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_venues">\n            Music and venues\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Music and venues">\n             edit\n            </a>\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h3>\n          <p>\n           The Hampton Roads region has a thriving music scene, with a heavy concentration thereof in the Virginia Beach, Chesapeake, and Norfolk areas. Many clubs, venues, and festivals exist within the region, all playing host to a wide variety of musical styles. There are a few hundred bands that play routinely in the region, spanning multiple genres. There are also twenty to thirty musical acts based in the region that perform throughout Hampton Roads and its surrounding areas on a "full-time" basis.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           In addition, plenty of well known acts have come from the area. Some of the major rock/pop artists include\n           <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Hornsby" title="Bruce Hornsby">\n            Bruce Hornsby\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gary_%22U.S.%22_Bonds" title=\'Gary "U.S." Bonds\'>\n            Gary "U.S." Bonds\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Juice_Newton" title="Juice Newton">\n            Juice Newton\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Mae" title="Mae">\n            Mae\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Seven_Mary_Three" title="Seven Mary Three">\n            Seven Mary Three\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Gene_Vincent" title="Gene Vincent">\n            Gene Vincent\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Keller_Williams" title="Keller Williams">\n            Keller Williams\n           </a>\n           , and\n           <a href="/wiki/Steve_Earle" title="Steve Earle">\n            Steve Earle\n           </a>\n           .\n           <a href="/wiki/Ella_Fitzgerald" title="Ella Fitzgerald">\n            Ella Fitzgerald\n           </a>\n           is the most recognizable jazz musician from the area.\n           <a href="/wiki/Robert_Cray" title="Robert Cray">\n            Robert Cray\n           </a>\n           and\n           <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Brown" title="Ruth Brown">\n            Ruth Brown\n           </a>\n           are both prominent blues and R&amp;B artists.\n           <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Newsom" title="Tommy Newsom">\n            Tommy Newsom\n           </a>\n           is another famous jazz musician. Many prominent rap and hip hop artists come from the area including\n           <a href="/wiki/Chad_Hugo" title="Chad Hugo">\n            Chad Hugo\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">\n            Clipse\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magoo_(rapper)" title="Magoo (rapper)">\n            Magoo\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">\n            Missy Elliott\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Wray" title="Nicole Wray">\n            Nicole Wray\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">\n            Pharrell Williams\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a href="/wiki/Quan_(rapper)" title="Quan (rapper)">\n            Quan\n           </a>\n           ,\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teddy_Riley_(producer)" title="Teddy Riley (producer)">\n            Teddy Riley\n           </a>\n           , and\n           <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">\n            Timbaland\n           </a>\n           .\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The region has a number of venues hosting live music and performances. Several of the larger (in order of maximum seating capacity) are:\n          </p>\n          <ul>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Veterans_United_Home_Loans_Amphitheater" title="Veterans United Home Loans Amphitheater">\n             Veterans United Home Loans Amphitheater\n            </a>\n            in Virginia Beach (seating 20,000)\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Scope" title="Norfolk Scope">\n             Norfolk Scope Arena\n            </a>\n            in Norfolk (seating 13,800)\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Coliseum" title="Hampton Coliseum">\n             Hampton Coliseum\n            </a>\n            in Hampton (seating 13,800)\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Kaplan_Arena" title="Kaplan Arena">\n             Kaplan Arena\n            </a>\n            in Williamsburg (seating 10,175)\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Ted_Constant_Convocation_Center" title="Ted Constant Convocation Center">\n             Ted Constant Convocation Center\n            </a>\n            at\n            <a href="/wiki/Old_Dominion_University" title="Old Dominion University">\n             Old Dominion University\n            </a>\n            in Norfolk (seating 9,500)\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Pavilion" title="Portsmouth Pavilion">\n             Portsmouth Pavilion\n            </a>\n            in Portsmouth (seating 7,500)\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Le_Palais_Royal_Theatre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Le Palais Royal Theatre (page does not exist)">\n             Le Palais Royal Theatre\n            </a>\n            at\n            <a href="/wiki/Busch_Gardens_Williamsburg" title="Busch Gardens Williamsburg">\n             Busch Gardens Williamsburg\n            </a>\n            in James City County (seating 5,600)\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Ferguson_Center_for_the_Arts" title="Ferguson Center for the Arts">\n             Ferguson Center for the Arts\n            </a>\n            in Newport News (seating 1,725 and 453 in 2 separate concert halls)\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Matoaka_Amphitheatre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lake Matoaka Amphitheatre (page does not exist)">\n             Lake Matoaka Amphitheatre\n            </a>\n            at\n            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_College_of_William_%26_Mary" title="The College of William &amp; Mary">\n             The College of William &amp; Mary\n            </a>\n            in Williamsburg (seating 1,700)\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_NorVa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The NorVa (page does not exist)">\n             The NorVa\n            </a>\n            in Norfolk (standing 1,500)\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n          <p>\n           Dozens of much smaller commercial establishments offer live music and other entertainment such as comedy shows and mystery dinner-theater throughout the region.\n          </p>\n          <h2>\n           <span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_recreation">\n            Parks and recreation\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hampton_Roads&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Parks and recreation">\n             edit\n            </a>\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h2>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Botanical_Garden" title="Norfolk Botanical Garden">\n            Norfolk Botanical Garden\n           </a>\n           , opened in 1939, is a 155-acre (0.6\xc2\xa0km\n           <sup>\n            2\n           </sup>\n           )\n           <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">\n            botanical garden\n           </a>\n           and\n           <a href="/wiki/Arboretum" title="Arboretum">\n            arboretum\n           </a>\n           located near the Norfolk International Airport. It is open year-round.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norfolk_Botanical_Gardens_89-0">\n            <a href="#cite_note-Norfolk_Botanical_Gardens-89">\n             [89]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Zoo" title="Virginia Zoo">\n            Virginia Zoological\n           </a>\n           Park, opened in 1900, is a 65-acre (260,000\xc2\xa0m\n           <sup>\n            2\n           </sup>\n           )\n           <a href="/wiki/Zoo" title="Zoo">\n            zoo\n           </a>\n           with hundreds of animals on display, including the critically endangered\n           <a href="/wiki/Siberian_tiger" title="Siberian tiger">\n            Siberian tiger\n           </a>\n           and threatened\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_rhino" title="White rhino">\n            white rhino\n           </a>\n           .\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Virginia_Zoo_90-0">\n            <a href="#cite_note-Virginia_Zoo-90">\n             [90]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           <a href="/wiki/First_Landing_State_Park" title="First Landing State Park">\n            First Landing State Park\n           </a>\n           and\n           <a href="/wiki/False_Cape_State_Park" title="False Cape State Park">\n            False Cape State Park\n           </a>\n           are both located in coastal areas in Virginia Beach. Both offer camping facilities, cabins, and outdoor recreation activities in addition to nature and history tours. First Landing is the site of\n           <a href="/wiki/Cape_Henry" title="Cape Henry">\n            Cape Henry\n           </a>\n           while False Cape is located at the southeastern end of Virginia Beach.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n            <a href="#cite_note-91">\n             [91]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n            <a href="#cite_note-92">\n             [92]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           <a href="/wiki/Newport_News_Park" title="Newport News Park">\n            Newport News Park\n           </a>\n           is located in the northern part of the city of Newport News. The city\'s golf course also lies within the park along with camping and outdoor activities. There are over 30 miles (48\xc2\xa0km) of trails in the Newport News Park complex. The park has a 5.3-mile (8.5-km) multi-use bike path. The park offers bicycle and helmet rental, and requires helmet use by children under 14. Newport News Park also offers an archery range, disc golf course, and an "aeromodel flying field" for remote-controlled aircraft, complete with a 400\xc2\xa0ft (120\xc2\xa0m) runway.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n            <a href="#cite_note-93">\n             [93]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           The region also has amusement parks which attract tourists and locals alike. The Virginia Beach Oceanfront has\n           <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Fun_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Atlantic Fun Park (page does not exist)">\n            Atlantic Fun Park\n           </a>\n           (formerly called "Virginia Beach Amusement Park"). Virginia Beach also has\n           <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ocean_Breeze_Waterpark&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ocean Breeze Waterpark (page does not exist)">\n            Ocean Breeze Waterpark\n           </a>\n           , Shipwreck Golf, and\n           <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Motor_World&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Motor World (page does not exist)">\n            Motor World\n           </a>\n           which were formerly combined into one as "Ocean Breeze Fun Park". As separate parks, they provide miniature golf, go-karts, water slides, pools, climbing wall, paintball area, and kiddie rides.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n            <a href="#cite_note-94">\n             [94]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n            <a href="#cite_note-95">\n             [95]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n           <a href="/wiki/Busch_Gardens_Williamsburg" title="Busch Gardens Williamsburg">\n            Busch Gardens Williamsburg\n           </a>\n           and\n           <a href="/wiki/Water_Country_USA" title="Water Country USA">\n            Water Country USA\n           </a>\n           are the major theme parks in Williamsburg.\n          </p>\n          <h2>\n Douglas Wilder Performing Arts Center\n            </a>\n            at Norfolk State University \xe2\x80\x93 Norfolk\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            Portsmouth Pavilion- Portsmouth, \xe2\x80\x93 Williamsburg\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            The Push Comedy Theater \xe2\x80\x93 Norfolk\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n          <h2>\n           <span Newspapers\n           </span>\n           <span class="mw-editsection">\n            <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n             [\n            </span>\n            <a       ]\n            </span>\n           </span>\n          </h3>\n          <p>\n           Three daily newspapers serve Hampton Roads:\n           <i>\n            <a href="/wiki/The_Virginian-Pilot" title="The Virginian-Pilot">\n             The Virginian-Pilot\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           in the Southside, the\n           <i>\n            <a href="/wiki/Daily_Press_(Virginia)" title="Daily Press (Virginia)">\n             Daily Press\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           on the Peninsula, and the six days a week\n           <i>\n            <a href="/wiki/Suffolk_News-Herald" title="Suffolk News-Herald">\n             Suffolk News-Herald\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           that serves Suffolk and Franklin.\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hampton_Roads_News_Links_102-0">\n            <a href="#cite_note-Hampton_Roads_News_Links-102">\n             [102]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n           Smaller publications include the Williamsburg-James City County area\'s twice-weekly\n           <i>\n            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Gazette" title="Virginia Gazette">\n             Virginia Gazette\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           (the state\'s oldest newspaper\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n            <a href="#cite_note-103">\n             [103]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n           ), the\n           <i>\n            <a href="/wiki/New_Journal_and_Guide" title="New Journal and Guide">\n             New Journal and Guide\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           , and\n           <i>\n            <a href="/wiki/Inside_Business_(newspaper)" title="Inside Business (newspaper)">\n             Inside Business\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           , the area\'s only business newspaper.\n          </p>\n          <p>\n           Newspapers serving the Hampton Roads area include:\n          </p>\n      </i>\n            \xe2\x80\x93\n            <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n             Williamsburg\n            </a>\n           </li>\n
